Current Affairs Commentary

Ideas on Rectifying Overseas Consulates

A nation's permanent overseas personnel consist of diplomats and consuls, distinct from each other. The consul's duty is solely to protect overseas citizens and develop commerce. In countries without a native ambassador, consuls may also serve as the nation's foreign representative. While the status of a consul may not be equal to that of a diplomat, they still receive special protection under international law. Public documents under their care enjoy inviolable sanctity, and they are exempt from conscription and direct taxation in their host country. According to international convention, consuls must first receive recognition from the head of the host country to officially exercise their duties. If they engage in illegal or improper conduct, the head of the host country can revoke their recognition, indirectly removing them from office. Therefore, in the strictest sense, a consul is actually subject to the control of both their home country and the host country, serving as an official of both. Their responsibility is thus quite significant.

The responsibilities of a Chinese consul today likely surpass those of their foreign counterparts. Chinese citizens are spread worldwide, and they have consistently provided significant assistance to the nation's economy, patriotic movements, and domestic charitable causes. In today's global economic downturn, anti-Chinese tragedies continue to occur. How can the government stand idly by? The importance of consular affairs cannot be ignored – this is the first point. Imported goods flood the market, with loopholes needing to be plugged. Domestic goods sell poorly, lacking vitality. To develop international trade, accurate and timely on-site information is essential. The importance of consular affairs cannot be ignored – this is the second point. The National Government recognizes this and has implemented measures such as cargo manifest certifications to supplement consular funding and rigorous examinations to carefully select consular officials. All of these are fundamental and self-evident. What I wish to discuss are matters no less important than funding and personnel selection, but which the authorities may not be giving sufficient attention to, or which, although the authorities have experimented with, have not been continuously promoted, and are therefore specifically highlighted.

(1) Formulation of Service Regulations. The tasks of a consul can be broadly divided into four categories: (A) developing commerce; (B) protecting overseas citizens; (C) supervising ships; and (D) other miscellaneous tasks. Under these general categories, the events that need to be handled are extraordinarily complex. For example, under category (A): monitoring whether domestic and host country commerce is faithfully executed, investigating the economic conditions, financial markets, and people's preferences of the host country and its neighboring areas, etc. Under category (B): paying attention to the entry and departure of domestic ships, mediating or arbitrating disputes between crew members and sailors or passengers, etc. Under category (C): handling citizen registration, inventorying and protecting the estates of the deceased, etc. Under category (D): certifying wills, witnessing weddings, issuing passports, and certifying cargo manifests, etc. Our current consular service regulations are fragmented and incomplete compared to the comprehensive and detailed regulations of foreign countries. For example, very few overseas Chinese make wills, and their registration at the consulate is often incomplete and inaccurate. If an overseas Chinese citizen dies, it is often impossible to determine who their legal heirs are. If the consul does not investigate and protect their estate, the earnings of their lifetime of labor will inevitably be confiscated by the local government and vanish without a trace. However, our government lacks detailed regulations to guide consular operations. Even those who are enthusiastic about serving will inevitably feel lost and helpless. This situation is ubiquitous overseas, and the losses of overseas Chinese property are countless. It is truly lamentable. This one example illustrates the rest.

(2) Promotion of Civil Registration. Many overseas Chinese leave their homeland due to economic hardship or restrictive immigration policies, leaving their families behind. If an accident occurs and they need to prove their relationship with relatives in the country, it is extremely difficult. Our new civil registration system has not been in place for long, and those in charge are perfunctory and irresponsible, regarding it as unimportant. Therefore, consuls who wish to protect the legal interests of overseas Chinese relatives often lack evidence to prove their identity and can only regret their powerlessness. Sometimes, the host country's authorities may be lenient, but the consulate must still painstakingly seek appropriate evidence from the country to gain the trust of foreigners and protect its own prestige. Therefore, the failure to implement civil registration is a national disgrace that harms overseas citizens, causing endless trouble and wasting time. While it is impossible to implement this nationwide simultaneously without any shortcomings, overseas Chinese are most numerous in the provinces of Fujian and Guangdong, and their ancestral homes are mostly located along the coasts of these two provinces. Implementing civil registration within this small area may not be too difficult. Moreover, once properly implemented, it will benefit the improvement of local administration, not only facilitating consular operations but also benefiting overseas Chinese communities.

(3) Holding Circuit Performance Evaluations. The National Government's Ministry of Foreign Affairs previously sent personnel to inspect consulates in Southeast Asia, which was quite beneficial diplomatically. However, this has not been extended to other regions, which is regrettable. In the future, we should follow the examples of other countries and commission impartial and capable personnel to regularly inspect the performance of each consulate and their relationships with local officials and overseas citizens in the host country, as a basis for rewards and punishments.

Major Bloodshed in French Corruption Scandal

Daladier Government Overthrown

Hundreds Dead and Wounded in Dark Night Battles in Paris

Royalist Uprising and Communist Rebellion

(Paris) The Daladier cabinet has just submitted its resignation. (Havas dispatch, 7th)

(Paris) French Premier Daladier went to the Presidential Palace this afternoon to resign as Prime Minister to avoid further bloodshed. Daladier won in the Chamber of Deputies but failed in the streets. There were rumors of a general resignation this morning. According to unconfirmed reports, Daladier met with the President to discuss declaring a state of alert. Opposition leaders Tettio and Laval are currently drafting a declaration to the speakers of both houses of parliament. The vote in the Chamber of Deputies yesterday indicated that the government is socialist in nature rather than unified. With Daladier's resignation, France is now without a cabinet. Former President Doumer, although re-invited to form a cabinet in the previous nine days, declined. It is widely believed that the President will advocate dissolving parliament and holding new elections, hoping to eliminate the socialist majority. Before resigning, Daladier consulted with Interior Minister Frot, who agreed to implement the most effective plan today to deal with the rioters. Daladier stated that the government is responsible for maintaining order but does not want to use bloodshed to suppress or use troops to deal with demonstrators. Herriot attended the meeting between Daladier and Frot. (Reuters dispatch, 7th)

(Paris) Premier Daladier issued a statement late at night detailing the riots, saying, "This is an attempt by certain political groups to overthrow the republican system through violent coups. The rioters carried knives and guns and attacked police and guards. A detailed examination of those arrested proves that this is a violent act detrimental to national security. Fortunately, the defense was strong, and the rioters did not achieve their purpose. The government is determined to safeguard the safety of the people and the independence of the republican system by legal means and hopes that people across the country will cooperate." (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

(Paris) This morning, the authorities issued a statement saying that six people died and 400 were injured and hospitalized in yesterday's riots, with demonstrators and police accounting for half each. Countless others suffered minor injuries and were treated at home. A total of 350 people were arrested during the riots and will be charged with inciting murder and conspiring to endanger national security. (Reuters dispatch, 7th)

(Paris) After the news of the fall of the Daladier government spread, crowds gathered again on Concorde Street and Royal Street. Police officers frequently used batons to disperse them, but the crowds remained and some threw bricks and stones, making the situation increasingly tense. (Reuters dispatch, 7th)

Fires Erupt Throughout Paris, French Government Surrounded

Rioters and Police and Military Fight Like Demons

Injured Lie Strewn Across the Streets, Blood-Stained Clothing Scattered

Cleared Only After Midnight with Gunfire

(Paris) After a day of tension, Parisian workers gradually left their offices and factories at dusk. An hour later, the streets were filled with demonstrators, who threw glass objects at mounted patrols. Crowds along the roadside also set off firecrackers to boost their morale. At that time, the mounted patrols maintained order in a friendly manner. Shortly thereafter, communists set fire to tobacco shops, newspaper stands, and motorcycles. The situation then became tense. Guards had to use bayonets to charge at the stone-throwing rioters, but they were outnumbered and retreated. The rioters gradually advanced to the iron fence outside the Chamber of Deputies, and the French government was surrounded. Although several injured people were carried into the hospital, no one inside was allowed to leave. At the time, several right-wing city councilors marched down Rivoli Road, hoping to position themselves in front of the crowd. The most intense riot started with the battle on the Concorde Bridge in the evening. The rioters surged like a tide, and the police and Republican Guard were unable to resist. After occupying the bridge, the rioters trapped the police and were unable to stop the arson of motorcycles and private cars.

Crowds also set fires in other parts of the city and threw stones at police detachments. They also destroyed cafes on several historically valuable streets. The Faubourg Saint-Honoré was filled with injured people, broken glass, and blood-stained clothing. The main forces of the riot were royalists, industrial revolution unions, communists, socialists, etc. Their party newspapers all encouraged them to vigorously oppose the Stavisky corruption scandal. The riot first broke out in front of the City Hall, with the crowd shouting "Down with the government!" and "Down with Chiappe!" Seeing the crowds surging, cafe owners quickly cleared the chairs and tables from the roadside, and stores closed their doors and stored all glass objects. At 9 p.m., a team of rioters set fire to the Ministry of the Navy at the corner of Concorde Street and Royal Street. The fire brigade rushed to the scene from streets crowded with people and extinguished the fire within thirty minutes, but several houses had already been destroyed.

At 11 p.m., two battalions of infantry were stationed in front of the Chamber of Deputies. The soldiers all carried dry rations so that they could be stationed there all night. When the police guarding the Concorde Bridge were forced back several steps by the rioters, they fired pistols and then began a fierce fight. The mounted patrol charged six times. Reuters reporters saw at least fifteen mounted patrolmen's heads smashed by rioters with sticks and stones. The two sides advanced and retreated repeatedly, fighting like demons.

The second half of the riot was a battle between veterans and the Republican Guard. The veterans marched onto the scene in formation at 9:40 p.m., led by flag bearers, and a fight broke out immediately. Two fire hoses were used to spray water at them, but the old warriors did not give in. Two motorcycles on Concorde Street were burning fiercely, and no one cared. The street was filled with shoes, hats, torn clothes, broken glasses, etc. At the time, the shouts and trumpet sounds of the crowd were mixed with a strange, sharp sound, as gas lamps were broken and gas leaked out. Police officers with pistols fired along Concorde Street to drive away the crowd until after midnight. Hundreds of injured people were lying on the streets, several of whom were seriously injured. The police had tried their best to restrain themselves today, but when the rioters attacked the Concorde Bridge, the patrol team fired several volleys, killing a woman.

Several places such as Lyon, Marseille, Lille, and Nancy also had demonstrations and minor riots today.

At 1:10 this morning (Wednesday), the Prime Minister held a military meeting at the Ministry of Interior. Interior Minister Frot and other cabinet members attended. Frot gave a speech thanking the police for their efforts in suppressing the riot. At 1:40 this morning, the Concorde Street and other streets were quiet, but rioters were still demonstrating in Royal Street and other places. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Royalists Forcefully Storm Chamber of Deputies, Parliament Turns into Hospital

Right-Wing Demonstrations and Communist Counter-Demonstrations

City Councilors Also Lead Crowds to Attack

Injured People's Eyeballs Burst Out, Others Arrested

(Paris) Tonight, far-right royalists demonstrated near the Chamber of Deputies, and the scope quickly expanded. The demonstrators repeatedly tried to break into the Chamber, but were stopped by guerrilla guards. In other areas, right-wing demonstrators encountered communist counter-demonstrators and clashed.

In front of the Tuileries Palace, demonstrators overturned three buses and seized roadside trees, benches, and streetlights to throw at the police. Deputy Inspector Marchand was injured.

Another team of demonstrators, led by eight members of the Paris City Council, set out from the City Hall and marched towards the Chamber of Deputies, resulting in a clash with the police. Two city councilors were seriously injured, one with an eyeball bursting out. All eight were arrested.

At 10:30 p.m., demonstrations broke out again on the Place de la Concorde. Right-wing people and communists clashed with each other. The police tried their best to disperse them. The Beaujon Hospital received 43 injured people, two of whom had already died, and seven others were critically injured. The number of injured people received by the Laennec Hospital and the Municipal Hospital was roughly the same, but there were no deaths yet. After the Chamber of Deputies adjourned, the government held a cabinet meeting in the Chamber. Due to the large number of deaths and injuries, it was decided to file public charges for the crimes of ordering murder and conspiring to undermine national security. After the parliament adjourned, the clerks extinguished the lights and opened the side doors so that members and observers could leave. In front of the main gate, the fire brigade used water hoses to prevent the demonstrators from advancing. A temporary military hospital was set up inside the Chamber to treat injured police and soldiers. Finally, the demonstration gradually weakened, but a large battalion of infantry was still stationed in front of the Chamber to prevent any surprises. Demonstrations also occurred in provinces such as Lyon and Rouen, but the situation was not serious. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

(Paris) Maurras, the editor of the royalist newspaper "Action Française," published an article yesterday, deliberately causing trouble. The court has decided to prosecute him for inciting murder. (Havas dispatch, 7th)

New Cabinet Wins Confidence After Shouting and Cheering in Chamber of Deputies

Daladier Handles the Situation Calmly

Vote of Confidence Passed by Three Votes

(Paris) When Premier Daladier read out the declaration of the new government's major policies in the Chamber of Deputies today, the shouts and cheers in the hall were deafening, making it impossible to finish reading. This is unprecedented in the history of France's parliamentary system. The Speaker announced a ten-minute recess. When the meeting reconvened, the members were still very agitated. Daladier maintained the overall situation with a humorous demeanor. When the members returned to the hall, Daladier played with his hat, gesturing as if to say, "Gentlemen, if you are quiet, we can proceed with the meeting; otherwise, I will put on my hat and leave." The first gathering of the Chamber was almost immediately disrupted by the noise. When the cabinet members entered the hall, some on the left cheered, while those on the right shouted insults. Others were insulted by the left and cheered by the right. When Daladier read the declaration, the left cheered and the right shouted insults. As the members filed in, several Socialist and Radical Party members attacked several right-wing members. The hall guards used all their strength to separate the two sides. The visitors' gallery was full, and admission tickets were strictly checked 100 yards from the parliament. No one without a ticket was allowed to enter.

After the second gathering, Daladier finished reading his declaration and allowed only four members of the opposition to raise questions as a vote of confidence. The declaration, in addition to expressing the determination to maintain the gold standard and international cooperation, also promised that the parliamentary committee would investigate the Stavisky fraud case. Daladier also stated loudly that at a time when all of Europe is in turmoil and division, national defense is of utmost importance. We must not be confused and indecisive, bearing the blame for France falling into a new catastrophe with the rest of Europe. As for the meeting system, it should be well protected, the accounting system must be reformed, and the budget must be passed by March 31.

After Daladier finished his speech, the members voted on the motion of confidence after debating it, which passed by 300 votes to 217 votes.

The Chamber of Deputies was adjourned immediately. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Paris Resembles Battlefield After Night of Bloodshed

Still in a State of Turmoil

Number of Demonstrators Close to 50,000

(Paris) Paris's beautiful Concorde Street now resembles a battlefield after a night of riots and bloodshed. Paris is still in an extremely unsettled state. Concorde Street is full of iron bars, iron pipes, bricks, and stones. It is estimated that the number of rioters is close to 50,000. The traces of destruction in the streets are enough to prove the intensity of the riot. The exterior is now protected by squads of infantry. Newspapers said that the demonstrators were mixed with communists, which caused the change. "Action Française," one of the famous political dailies, has been confiscated today. The official statement of the number of deaths and injuries in last night's disturbance is: six civilians dead, three guards missing, 170 civilians injured, 180 police injured, and 230 guards injured. Barton, the Undersecretary of National Education, resigned today. Right-wing opposition leaders have put forward a motion requesting an immediate investigation into last night's events. Paris is superficially calm now, but the atmosphere is very tense. Those who went to Concorde Street and other places for inspection this afternoon were all monitored by the police and not allowed to stay, in order to comply with the order prohibiting gatherings. There were no further disturbances or arrests at 1 p.m. (Reuters dispatch, 7th)

(Paris) During last night's riots in Paris, an American girl was killed by a stray bullet. The Paris police chief and the famous aviator Major Herteau were also seriously injured. At the time, the crowd shouted, "Send Chiappe to prison!" and "Shoot Daladier!" After the Chamber of Deputies adjourned, the members could not leave because demonstrators were gathered outside, and the police could not guarantee the safety of the members leaving the Chamber. At the time, more than sixty injured police officers were carried into the Chamber to treat their wounds. (National Telegram, 7th)

Process of Daladier Cabinet's General Resignation

Former President Doumer Declined to Form Cabinet

(Paris) This afternoon, Premier Daladier and all cabinet members resigned. After last night's riot, Socialist leader Blum and Socialist extremist leader Herriot met with Daladier and persuaded him to resign. Daladier then convened a meeting of all cabinet members. The truth of this incident is due to the dismissal of former Police Commissioner Chiappe and the repercussions of the Bayonne swindle case. Therefore, in order to avoid further riots or bloodshed, it was decided to resign en masse. As a result of last night's riot, approximately sixteen people died and one hundred and fifty-four were injured. (National Telegram, 7th)

(Paris) At 1:30 p.m., Premier Daladier left the Prime Minister's Office and announced to the press that the cabinet had submitted its general resignation, but declined to issue any other statement. Subsequently, President Lebrun re-entrusted former President Doumer with the organization of a new cabinet, but Doumer again refused to accept the mandate. (Havas dispatch, 7th)

British and American Troops Stationed in Peiping Practice Target Shooting

(Peiping) More than 70 American infantry and cavalry stationed in Peiping went out of the Dongbianmen this morning to the area of Prince Yu's tomb in the eastern suburbs to practice live-fire shooting. In addition, more than 50 British soldiers, carrying two machine guns, practiced target shooting in Miaojiadi. (Special Dispatch, 7th)

British Parliament Debates Disarmament

Simon Declaration Endeavors to Mediate

Serious Differences Remain in the Development of the Situation

Eden Travels to France, Germany, and Italy to Exchange Views

(London) British Foreign Secretary Simon began the world-attracting disarmament debate in the House of Commons today. The House was extremely crowded, and many members of the diplomatic corps attended as observers.

Simon declared that since December 21, the situation has progressed, and the four countries of Britain, France, Italy, and Germany have all published important documents. Therefore, the situation has reached a point where a beneficial discussion can be held. Although serious differences still exist today, there has been a greater rapprochement on common grounds. Britain has received sufficient encouragement to continue to work for reconciliation, which is why Britain issued its memorandum on January 31.

The key to disarmament lies in the mutual concessions of France and Germany. Germany's demand for equality in armaments cannot be rejected and should not be rejected, because there can be no world peace if a great country and nation is kept in a subordinate position for a long time. If an urgent solution cannot be obtained, based on each country immediately abandoning its various war equipment that Germany is not allowed to possess, if an agreement cannot be reached quickly, Britain will have to consider its own armament, because Britain has no other way to stand in a world of endless armament.

All Countries Are in Danger If Disarmament Fails

British Plan Can Be a Basis for Compromise Simon also said that the British memorandum is by no means an ideal plan that disregards the needs and anxieties of others, but is presented to the world in a pragmatic spirit. Today, the times are increasingly contrary to those who advocate disarmament. The British plan is intended to lay the foundation for a swift compromise.

The British Foreign Secretary referred to Germany's rearmament, saying that any convention must accommodate Germany's rearming to some extent, but if equal rights are granted without reducing armaments in any aspect, this agreement will not be welcomed by the British government. Britain does not want to join any new constraints that would lead to coercive action regardless of the circumstances. Britain will do its best to faithfully fulfill its existing obligations.

After stating the obligation of the signatory countries to cooperate unanimously to prevent breaches of contract, Simon declared that the British proposal is a genuine progress. The next step is to make people all over the world fully understand the British memorandum and to fully understand the difficulties of other relevant countries. Therefore, the British government is now prepared to appoint the Lord Privy Seal to travel to Paris, Rome, and Berlin as soon as possible to explain Britain's position and to inquire about the opinions of other governments on the British memorandum. Eden could have set off immediately to France, but the political situation in France made people consider whether this trip would be convenient for France.

Simon concluded by saying that Britain's automatic implementation of its desire for disarmament has given the world extremely obvious evidence, and it is still its responsibility to launch it again. Britain is determined to promote an international agreement, regardless of the difficulties, and to consolidate the structure of world peace by all possible means, so that it and other countries can be spared the danger and burden that an unsettled agreement will inevitably lead to.

Japan's Invasion of China Shakes World Peace

Labor and Liberal Party Members of Parliament

Criticize Government's Disarmament Proposals

Labor Party leader Attlee stated that recognizing Germany's equality is too late and constitutes a concession to force rather than justice. The League of Nations' policy encourages countries to withdraw from the League and advocate for war in the hope of gaining rights. Japan has become a model for all countries in the world. The world cannot extend its authority in the Sino-Japanese dispute. The idea of security has been swept away. What the Labor Party wants is security and complete disarmament. The current British plan will not achieve this goal within the next ten years.

Liberal Party leader Samuel declared that the British proposal is uninspiring. He welcomes the agreement with Italy to improve the League of Nations. As for allowing Germany to rearm to some extent, it is an inevitable result of the principle of equality. This is not a surrender to Hitler, as all previous German governments have made this request. If the British plan is fully implemented, it could reduce armaments in Europe, but even if Europe agrees, there is no certainty in the Far East. Japan's attitude is almost completely opposed to disarmament. Japan has not yet indicated its acceptance of the proposed conditions. He hopes that the British government will not stop its progress due to the opposition of one country. He further hopes in a friendly spirit that the Japanese government will calmly consider its position, as Japan is diplomatically isolated due to its attitude towards Manchuria, economically due to its current situation in world trade, and morally and strategically due to its unique dissent and opposition to the general disarmament convention.

Conservative Party member Campbell advocated eliminating the causes of war, such as poorly managed borders, and suggested establishing a League of Nations court to handle complaints, with an international air force to enforce its authority. As for naval armaments, only cruisers of 8,000 tons or less are needed.

Warning to Germany Not to Violate the Independence of Neighboring Countries

The British Government Does Not Relinquish Trusteeship

Simon Only Acknowledges Equality of Rights

Former Foreign Secretary Austen Chamberlain stated that the agreement between Germany and Poland has not been lifted. Germany's obligations under the League of Nations Covenant, the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and the Locarno Treaties have not only not been relieved but have increased. This is very satisfying. It would be even more satisfying if Germany did not want to have anything to do with Austria at the same time. Germany should be given appropriate warning that the acceptance of Germany's demands must be conditional, that is, Germany must not use the strength of its armaments or the power of propaganda to express aggression against the independence of any other country, as Italy does. The former Foreign Secretary's words were met with applause. Chamberlain also said that it is now appropriate to ask Germany to frankly explain its wishes so that other countries can clearly indicate their limits. As for Germany's request for the return of its former colonies, the British government has no right to relinquish its trusteeship. If we must accept Germany's other demands, then Germany must withdraw such requests in order to reach an agreement. The Foreign Secretary Simon's statement that Germany's demand for equality of armaments cannot be rejected is dangerous, he believes. He hopes that Simon will deny that this statement implies that Germany's equality of naval armaments is also acceptable. The government party cheered loudly upon hearing this.

Foreign Secretary Simon then rose and said that if he had indeed used the term "equality of armaments," it was inappropriate. His original intention was to explain what was stated in the memorandum on armaments. The memorandum has already explained that the navy is a matter for separate negotiation. Lord Privy Seal Eden, on behalf of the government, replied that if Austria has decided to submit its dispute with Germany to the League of Nations, then this case is now in effect under trial. The actions to be taken in the future should be decided by the League of Nations Council. In joint action, Austria has the right to demand that any other country not interfere in its internal affairs. Eden also said that the British government fully agrees with the Italian government that Germany's return to Geneva to rejoin the League of Nations is the most important thing. He concluded by saying that the British government has asked other governments to accept the disarmament proposal as soon as possible, because accepting it at this time can bring the greatest political benefit to the world and generate the greatest trust among people. The government moved to adjourn the meeting, and the House of Commons agreed, ending the debate. (Transmitted by Central News Agency on the 6th)

Austrian Prime Minister Visits Hungary

Speculation About the Purpose of This Trip Varies

This morning, Vienna’s Prime Minister Dollfuss set off for the Hungarian capital, accompanied by the Director of the External Political Affairs Department, Paul Berlas, and the Hungarian Envoy to Austria. The “Federal Postal Newspaper” commented on the Prime Minister’s trip, stating that the joint policy of the two countries aims solely at unity and cooperation and is by no means directed against any country. The “New Vienna Newspaper” stated that Italy has granted Austria and Hungary trade access through the Italian port of Trieste to the Adriatic Sea. This grant of rights will be expressed by the Italian side during the Prime Minister's visit (Havas dispatch from the 7th).

Hungary and Russia Resume Diplomatic Relations

Both Parties Exchange Notes in Rome

Litvinov Negotiates Revival During Italian Tour

The Little Entente Will Follow Suit and Recognize Soviet Russia

(Moscow) The Soviet Ambassador to Italy, Potemkin, and the Hungarian Envoy to Turkey, Jung, exchanged notes in the Soviet Embassy in Italy, establishing normal diplomatic relations between the two countries. (TASS dispatch from the 6th)

The Rome agreement to resume diplomatic relations between Hungary and Russia was formally signed in Rome this Tuesday. According to this negotiation, the treaty was agreed upon after it began in Berlin in 1924, but it was never ratified. The Rome negotiations were initiated by Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov during his brief stay in the Holy City on his way back to Russia from the United States. (National News Agency dispatch from the 7th)

Rome. Hungary has officially recognized Soviet Russia, but Soviet Russia will not dispatch a diplomatic representative to the Hungarian capital until January of next year. During this time, Hungary will send Jung to Moscow. (Havas dispatch from the 7th)

Budapest. According to general speculation, Hungary's recognition of the Soviet Union is due to Italy's actions. The negotiations for Hungary's recognition of the Soviet Union were held in Rome, and the countries of the Little Entente are preparing to recognize the Soviet Union. This time, Hungary's recognition of the Soviet Union is intended to precede the countries of the Little Entente. Moreover, since the Moscow government has approached Hungary in the West, it can eventually join the League of Nations. From an economic point of view, although Hungary does not benefit much from recognizing the Soviet Union, Hungary can purchase some raw materials previously imported from the countries of the Little Entente from Russia in the future. In addition, agricultural machinery, electric seeders, and livestock produced by Hungary can be exported to Russia. (Havas dispatch from the 7th)

(Berlin) The German newspapers consider the restoration of diplomatic relations between Russia and Hungary to be of great significance, stating that this move is very gratifying and that Hungary's action is in line with Germany's consistent policy towards Russia. (Havas dispatch from the 7th)

Anglo-Japanese Cotton Industry Conference

To Be Held in London on the 12th of This Month

Japanese Economic League's Statement to Britain

Encouraging Britain with Coexistence and Co-prosperity

(Tokyo) The Japan Textile Federation received a report from its representative in the United Kingdom, Okada, that British representative Wilson visited Okada yesterday to discuss the steps for holding Anglo-Japanese cotton industry consultations. It was decided to hold the first meeting on the 12th of this month. Japanese Commercial Affairs Participant Makiyama will also participate. (China United Press dispatch from the 7th)

(Tokyo) Because the Anglo-Japanese consultations will be held soon, the Japan Economic League, on the 6th, sent a letter to various British parties in the name of the League President, Seinosuke Go, detailing the trade and financial relations between Japan and Britain. The reason why Japanese goods enter the European market is not intentional. Japan does not hesitate to control trade to uphold the spirit of coexistence, co-prosperity, and world peace. The last paragraph states that although we do not imagine that free trade can be realized in modern times, we do not doubt that separatist economics will lead to more tragic results. Now the world is at such a crossroads, and Japan and Britain are the Eastern and Western players repelling separatist economicism. Under this concept, we are pleased with the recent establishment of the Indo-Japanese consultations and sincerely hope that the upcoming Anglo-Japanese consultations will be successful. (United Press dispatch from the 7th)

Roosevelt's Focus Shifts to War Debts

Two Measures Are Proposed

Forceful Recovery and the Establishment of Trade Agreements

U.S. and Russia Will Begin Debt Negotiations in Geneva

(Washington) According to reliable sources, President Roosevelt plans to deliver a message to Congress today, specifically discussing the war debt issue. Although the content of the message has not been announced in detail, it is generally speculated that the President is unwilling to cancel or reduce the war debts. The President's new proposal is to first obtain the support of Congress and then contact the debtor countries. As a result of recent studies by the President and experts, it is generally felt that the current situation offers little hope of recovering war debts. If war debts are to be recovered, there are only two ways: one is by force, and the other is by trade agreement. The first method is the economic boycott of the debtor countries proposed by former Representative Johnson. This proposal is currently being discussed in the House Foreign Affairs Committee and is likely to pass in the House in the future. The second method has not yet been determined, but the President has consulted with financial and agricultural advisors several times in the past two weeks, intending to conclude trade agreements with the debtor countries to export America's surplus agricultural products abroad and to increase America's foreign trade. (National News Agency dispatch from the 6th)

(Washington) There is talk of Russia and the United States opening debt negotiations. Today, it was heard that more than a thousand citizens and companies petitioned the State Department to demand compensation for losses from Russia during the negotiations. The companies, because the products in Russia are owned by Soviet Russia, are requesting a total of $65 million in compensation for losses. Other requests include the repayment of Russian government bonds purchased by private individuals in the United States before the United States entered the European war. (Reuters dispatch from the 7th)

International Journalist William Martin Passes Away

Quite Capable of Upholding Justice in the Sino-Japanese Case

(Geneva) Dr. William Martin, former editor of the Geneva Newspaper and now professor of political science at the University of Zurich, passed away here today from pneumonia at the age of forty-six. Dr. Martin was a veteran of the European press. He upheld public opinion and adhered to justice throughout his life. When the Sino-Japanese dispute was submitted to the League of Nations for discussion, the Japanese tried their best to spread propaganda unfavorable to China in various newspapers. Only this newspaper upheld justice and fully announced the truth of the Japanese invasion of the Northeast, which benefited China greatly. Dr. Martin also wrote a book, "Japan and the League of Nations in Opposition," which expounded on Japan's morbid state of holding the League of Nations hostage in great detail. In the autumn of the year before last, Dr. Martin came to China at the invitation of various Chinese universities to give lectures, which were warmly welcomed by the audience. His sudden death is mourned by all who hear of it. (World News Agency dispatch from the 7th)

New Revolution Brewing in Spain

Madrid's Atmosphere Grows Tense Again

The atmosphere here in Madrid has become tense again, and there are fears that disturbances will occur again soon. Since the general election last November, the Labor Party has been trying to unite the Socialist Party, the Communist Party, and various industrial revolutionary factions to form a general front. Some have already been established in Catalonia and other places. Within the past week, several towns have announced general strikes. Except for bakeries and water and electricity plants, all work has been stopped, causing great inconvenience to the people. Recently, the number of unemployed people has continued to increase, and the activities of the revolutionary party have become more excited. Spain does not have a system of subsidizing the unemployed, so the unemployed and their families have no way to support themselves. It is said that thousands of households are crying out for food, which is extremely difficult. Many leaders of the Socialist Party, including several who have served as cabinet members, have joined the Labor Party. The failure of the Socialist Party in the general election last November was caused by the anxiety of the bourgeoisie and the middle class. The right-wing parties in Catalonia are now organizing informal defense corps to resist the violence of the industrial revolutionary faction. The government announced today that the authorities have made preparations to deal with all contingencies, but the cabinet is also facing many problems. Although the cabinet relies entirely on the support of the right wing, because the right wing is suspected of wanting to restore the monarchy, it has no representatives in the cabinet. For this reason, all urgently needed reforms have been stalled, and the right-wing members are also dissatisfied. A cabinet reshuffle to accommodate right-wing representatives seems inevitable, but once implemented, an explosion is to be feared. The Socialist Party issued a threat after the general election last November, saying that the real revolution had not yet arrived. This statement is still remembered today. (Reuters dispatch from the 7th)

Anglo-French Trade War Unavoidable

British Notice Expires on the 9th

France Still Shows No Sign of Changing Its Attitude

(London) Neither Britain nor France is willing to change its position. The trade war between the two countries is now closer than before. This was made clear in the British House of Commons today. Minister of Commerce Runciman stated in the House of Commons that there are currently no negotiations with France to conclude a new trade agreement. The British government does not want to negotiate on an unequal basis that discriminates against Britain. The British government is willing to strictly abide by the ten-day notice sent to France asking it to correct the discriminatory quota measures against Britain, partly because this declaration was issued before Daladier took office. If France takes no action to change its attitude during this period, Britain will take retaliatory measures to crack down on certain French goods. The British notice expires on February 9, but France has not yet shown any sign of changing its position, so negotiations are difficult to proceed. Although France has put forward several points for the British government to pay attention to, such as increasing the 1933 quota for certain British imports, France has not changed its attitude of reducing the British cloth import quota by 25%. At the beginning of this year, France reduced the import quota of British goods by 75%, which caused great indignation in Britain, which strongly protested against it. France then partially restored it, but Britain was still dissatisfied, because France had restored the original quota for the United States and other European countries, but not for Britain alone. (Reuters dispatch from the 6th)

Japanese House of Peers Questions Policy Toward Manchuria

The "Trinity" System Will Be Changed at the Appropriate Time

It Is Not Yet Time to End Military Operations

- Responses from the Foreign Minister and the Minister of War -

(Tokyo) Former Governor-General of Taiwan and member of the House of Peers, Eisuke Ishizuka, questioned the government's policy toward Manchuria this afternoon. The contents are as follows: (1) What is the government's fundamental policy toward Manchukuo? (2) The current situation, where the Commander of the Kwantung Army holds three positions concurrently, is no longer appropriate. Puyi has decided to become emperor on March 1, and the government should also adopt a policy of prioritizing military affairs and taking a civil administration policy. (3) It is rumored that after the Manchurian Incident, the military department advocated that internal policy must be reformed before going abroad and has drafted an internal reform plan. Is this a fact? (4) Regarding the issue of reforming the South Manchuria Railway, does the government have a finalized plan? Minister of War Hayashi said that the army has not drafted an internal reform plan and that it is not yet time to end military operations in Manchuria as soon as possible. Foreign Minister Hirota replied that the "Trinity" system will be changed at the appropriate time in the future. (China United Press dispatch from the 7th)

U.S. Authorities Deny Sino-American Aviation Secret Agreement

Japanese Foreign Minister Makes Reckless Speculation in Parliament

U.S. Private Companies Simultaneously Issue Statements to Refute Rumors

(Washington) Rumors that China and the United States had entered into a secret agreement to expand the Sino-American aviation business of the China National Aviation Corporation were ridiculed in official circles today as unfounded. This news was announced by Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota in the Japanese House of Peers. He also said that the territorial integrity treaty of China has been violated by the China National Aviation Corporation, and that this secret agreement is quite important for military operations. (National News Agency dispatch from the 6th)

(New York) Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota delivered a speech to the House of Peers today, saying that he strongly suspects that there is a secret agreement between the United States and China to develop Chinese aviation. Private American aviation companies, which jointly operate air transportation with the Chinese government, issued a statement after hearing Hirota's speech, saying, "The secret agreement mentioned by Hirota is indeed a secret, because we Americans have never heard of it." Representatives of these companies also said that the U.S. government has never participated in the contracts signed between the private companies and the Chinese government. According to the representatives, the reason why Japan feels uneasy is only because some American aviators who do not belong to the government voluntarily train Chinese flight personnel and are representatives of American aircraft manufacturers. In addition, the State Department also denied the Sino-American aviation secret agreement mentioned by Hirota. (Havas dispatch from the 6th)

He Zhuguo Arrives in Xinxiang

To Command the Suppression of Liu's Military

Fierce Fighting Occurs Around Panlingtai

Liu's Bandits Flee Southwest Toward Huixian

(Beiping) Xinxiang telegraph: He Zhuguo arrived in Xinxiang on the morning of the 7th to command the military suppression of bandits nearby. On the 6th, Liu's bandits fled to Panlingtai, more than 30 li north of Huixian City, where fierce fighting broke out with the Chang Jingwu Division and the horse regiment of He's army. Casualties on both sides were extremely heavy. Cavalry battalions of Qi Feng and Guo Xipeng and infantry battalions of Li and Shi were urgently dispatched to track and intercept them. The Cong Division and Yao Dongfan Division of the Chang Jingwu Division and the Kang artillery battalion were also sent to launch a head-on attack. Liu sent Zhou Yi with 3,000 yuan to comfort He's army's bandit suppression troops. Liu's bandits were ambushed by the Chang Jingwu horse regiment on the line of Liukui Gulch Guanyintang, north of Huixian, and casualties on both sides were extremely heavy. At noon on the 7th, Liu's bandits fled southwest toward the mountain road areas of Shimenkou and Bobi in Huixian County. Cavalry battalions of Wang Qifeng and infantry divisions of Chang Jingwu and Cong are being dispatched to take shortcuts to intercept them to the west. (Special dispatch from the 7th)

Yan Huiqing Arrives in Tianjin Yesterday

People of Tianjin Give a Warm Welcome

Yan Says There Is a Way Out in Diplomacy

(Tianjin) At 4:35 PM on the 7th, Ambassador to Russia Yan Huiqing arrived in Tianjin from Beijing. The train stopped at the new station for half an hour. The Provincial Government sent the Public Security Bureau Security Team to guard the station. Yu Xuezhong and members of the Provincial Committee boarded the train to welcome him. Dozens of Yan's old friends, Zhang Zhitian, Ni Daolang, etc., also boarded the train to meet him. Before the train left, Yan and Yu spoke with members of the Provincial Committee about his going to Russia nine months ago, actually traveling between Moscow and Geneva, and once going to Siberia in between. He lived in Russia for only six months. Because the delegation occupied the embassy, he worked out of hotels, spending many months living in hotels. Later, the embassy was vacated for repairs, which took another three months. The embassy's furniture was purchased from England, Germany, and within the country, and it took time to transport it. He had only just finished arranging it and moved in to work a few days before returning to the country. The upper floor of the embassy is for dormitories, and the lower floor is for public halls, almost like a large family. Russia can be said to be an ice-covered area. A few months ago, it had already reached minus 25 degrees Celsius, which is extremely cold. Before leaving the station, Yu and the Provincial Committee got off the train. At 5:05 PM, the train arrived at the east station. The Tianjin banking community, the business community,

The Nankai Alumni Association and students with flags welcomed him at the station. There were many people. Yan's two daughters jumped onto the train to see their father first. After Yan got off the train, he took his daughters in a car back to his private residence in Tianjin. The Tianjin reporter group boarded the train at the new station to visit Yan and followed him to the east station. On the train, Yan said that he had already given a talk to the press in Shanghai and Beijing, and had basically said what he wanted to say. He came to Tianjin to take care of personal matters and would go to Beiping in a few days, planning to stay at home for half a month, and then go to Beijing. He said that it was difficult to make a judgment about the poor relations between Japan and Russia, but the Europeans were extremely afraid of war and were trying to avoid it. Whether they could avoid it was another matter. We also hope that the relations between Japan and Russia will not break down and that they can settle things peacefully, which is human happiness. The Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan seems to be effective on the surface. It must be known that a country organized with an ideology is definitely stronger than one organized without an ideology. The treaty signed by Jin Shuren and Russia is naturally invalid because it has not been approved by the central government. He learned about this matter in the newspapers and has not yet received details after returning home. The saying that there is a way out in diplomacy is a personal research experience and cannot be exhausted in one sentence. He will announce it later. (Special dispatch from the 7th)

(Jinan) Yan Huiqing passed through Jinan this morning on his way to Tianjin, and Song Zheyuan's representative Xiao Xiangge also passed through Jinan on his way back to Chahar. (Special dispatch from the 7th)

The China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC) Concludes Agreement with Hong Kong Government

Hong Kong to Establish Aviation Station

Shanghai-Guangdong-Hong Kong-Philippines Route Completed

(Nanjing) Aviation circles report that the joint Shanghai-Guangdong-Hong Kong air transport has not yet been realized due to various obstacles. If it can be realized, the Sino-British-American air route will be unimpeded. The American Far East Company is also planning a route from Hong Kong to Hanoi, which will be connected to the British Imperial Airways in the future. As for the Shanghai-Guangdong-Hong Kong-Philippines route, Mr. Bi Shi Bi, a technician from the China National Aviation Corporation, went south to negotiate with the Hong Kong government and has successfully added Hong Kong as an aviation station. Since the China National Aviation Corporation opened the Shanghai-Guangdong civil aviation route, passengers and merchants traveling to and from Wenzhou, Fuzhou, Xiamen, Shantou, and Guangzhou have found it convenient. At that time, the company originally planned to establish an aviation station in Hong Kong, but it did not obtain the consent of the Hong Kong government at that time, so it first established the Shanghai-Guangdong route. In order to expedite the Hong Kong government's participation, the China National Aviation Corporation sent Mr. Bi Shi Bi south from Shanghai again to negotiate with the Hong Kong government several times. Now, after the two parties have exchanged opinions, they are very satisfied. After the draft treaty is finalized, Mr. Bi will return to Shanghai to report to the head office, and the formal signing will be carried out immediately. The Shanghai-Guangdong-Hong Kong and Manila routes can then be connected. (7th dispatch)

(Nanjing) With the Guangdong-Shaanxi route about to open, the Eurasia Aviation Corporation has requested the Ministry of Communications to establish a Changsha airport station. The Ministry of Communications has consulted the Hunan Provincial Government to assist in handling it. (7th dispatch)
