Local

Shanghai Children's Welfare Association

Actively Organizing Children's Services

▲Health Department and Nursery Group Held Meetings Yesterday

▲Child and Infant Health Guidance Centers to be Established in Nanshi and Zhabei

▲Yang Maorong to be Appointed as Director of the First Nursery

The Shanghai Children's Welfare Committee, to develop children's services, has designated this year as Children's Year and is actively preparing various programs. Yesterday, the Health Department and Nursery Group of the committee convened meetings to discuss all ongoing matters. Details of the meetings are recorded as follows:

▲First Meeting of the Health Department

The first meeting of the Health Department was held at the Dengtuomo Hotel at 12:00 noon yesterday. Over thirty people attended, including Pan Gongzhan, Li Tingan, Zhou Shang, Hu Shuyi, Wu Liguo, Wang Guanyi, Chen Bingqian, Xu Naili, Fu Wenshou, Chen Hongda, Gao Jinglang, Ling Xitao (represented by Qian Yiqin), Su Jielang, and Sun Jiaqi. Li Tingan chaired the meeting, and Zhou Shang served as the recorder. The chairman first reported the significance of convening this meeting and the future work steps. Then, Pan Gongzhan delivered a speech, and Wu Liguo and Xu Naili reported on the work status of the Zhabei clinic and the physical examination of children. The discussion then began on: (1) a proposal for the association to cooperate with all charitable child welfare organizations in Shanghai. It was resolved to appoint Pan Gongzhan and Li Tingan of the Children's Welfare Association, Wang Guanyi of the Chinese Charitable Child Welfare Association, Xu Naili of the Lianqing Society, and Su Jielang of the Family Industry Society as five members to review the cooperation methods. (2) The issue of determining the date of the meeting. It was decided to convene a meeting at the Lianhuan Society on Sanma Road at 4:30 p.m. on the ninth of this month. (3) The issue of how to raise funds for the Health Department. It was resolved that the general association would raise funds. After the discussion, Su Jielang, the director of the Children's Dental Hospital of the Family Industry Society, led a tour of the hospital, and the meeting adjourned.

▲Services Planned for This Year

The Health Department has set the following services to be organized in 1934: Establishing child and infant health guidance centers in Nanshi and Zhabei to handle (1) regular infant check-ups (under one year old), vaccinations, nutritional supplements and guidance, correction of deficiencies, bathing, maternal childcare guidance, and home visits; (2) pre-school children's hygiene, the development of hygienic habits, outdoor games and sunbathing; (3) school children, in addition to the full implementation of school health work in the city, it is planned to organize a summer camp for a period of one to two months in the summer of this year, with a limit of 300 people. The location will be at the Seaport Quarantine Hospital or any large private garden. According to Li Tingan, director of the Health Department, the project will first be launched in Zhabei and Nanshi, and will be expanded after it has achieved better results.

▲Second Regular Meeting of the Nursery Group

The Nursery Group held its second regular meeting at the Lianhuan Society at 4:30 p.m. yesterday. Pan Gongzhan, Wang Guanyi, Hu Shuyi, Yang Maorong, Qiu Xisheng, Chen Lengseng, Jiang Shicheng, Wu Liguo, Shen Tong (represented by Ma Guixin), Gao Jinglang, Chen Jicheng (represented by Xu Ruofang), Gong Yushuo, Yang Meibei, Yin Guanzhi, and Chen Bai attended. Wang Guanyi chaired the meeting, and Zhou Wanghe served as the recorder. Matters reported: (1) progress in preparing the location for the nursery; (2) fundraising and usage methods for the group's expenses; (3) a letter from the Social Affairs Bureau discussing the addition of a labor nursery when starting a nursery; (4) Committee Member Yang explained the floor plan of the recent Panfang building and the method of distribution and use. Following were matters for discussion: (1) the issue of the meeting place. It was resolved to ask Committee Member Hu Shuyi to propose to the association's standing committee for a decision and then hand it over to the group for discussion. (2) The issue of the person in charge of the First Nursery. It was resolved to invite Committee Member Yang Maorong to be the director of the First Nursery. (3) The issue of the honorary director of the First Nursery. It was resolved to submit it to the Standing Committee for discussion. (4) The issue of personnel for the nursery. It was resolved to ask Director Yang to draft a method and submit it to the general meeting for approval and decision. (5) The Social Affairs Bureau's letter discussing the group's devising ways to raise funds for the establishment of a labor nursery. It was resolved to ask Committee Members Qiu, Yin, and Chen to be responsible for contacting various factories to establish labor nursery funds and report to the association for discussion. (6) The issue of formulating all plans for the nursery. It was resolved to ask Director Yang to be responsible for drafting and submitting it to the general meeting for approval. (7) The issue of the number of people admitted to the nursery. It was resolved to temporarily set it at one hundred. After the discussion, Pan Gongzhan, chairman of the Standing Committee, gave a speech, and the meeting adjourned.

Pan Zhuqi Travels the World to Study Education

▲First to Italy, then to Soviet Russia

▲Expected to Return Home in About a Year

Pan Zhuqi, former director of education and construction in Guangxi Province and current president of Guangxi University and the Agricultural College, was recently ordered by the provincial government to travel the world to study industrial education. He recently arrived in Shanghai and informed us in detail about the recent situation in Guangxi and his itinerary. The details are recorded below:

Recent Situation of the University

Guangxi University was founded in 1928 and currently has more than 600 students. It was suspended for two years due to the 1929 political upheaval and was restored in 1931. Initially, it established three colleges of science, agriculture, and engineering. The president concurrently serves as the dean of the College of Engineering, and Mr. Pan concurrently serves as the dean of the College of Agriculture. Ma Minghai concurrently serves as the dean of the College of Science. The professors hired are all well-known scholars of the time, and they pay special attention to students' extracurricular activities. The equipment is comprehensive, and the education is excellent, deeply trusted by the Department of Education, and it is indeed the only perfect institution of higher learning in the southwest of our country.

Socializing in Beijing

After being ordered by the provincial government to go to various countries for inspection, Mr. Pan arrived in Shanghai by sea. Due to applying for a passport to go abroad, he made a special trip to Beijing a few days ago and met with Soviet Ambassador Bogomolov. Bogomolov expressed his welcome to Mr. Pan's visit to the country to inspect industries and was introduced by Consul General Spier to several letters of introduction to allow him to delve into the country for on-the-spot investigation. Since Mr. Pan will spend a longer time in Russia, it is necessary to conduct an in-depth investigation of the success of the Soviet Five-Year Plan and the substantial progress in industry. Mr. Pan also intends to conduct an accompanying investigation of education in the Soviet Union.

Itinerary and Dates

It is now scheduled to take the Italian liner Conte Rosso on the ninth of this month and go directly to Italy. After staying for about two weeks, he will go to Germany and then to Denmark in Northern Europe, then through Poland and to Soviet Russia. He will spend a very short time in the United Kingdom, France, Austria, and Switzerland, totaling about five months in Europe and about five months in Russia. He can return home at the end of this year.

Recent Situation in Guangxi

During the conversation, Mr. Pan expressed his satisfaction with Guangxi's administration, construction, and education. He said that students in various schools pay special attention to military training. In recent years, the people of Guangxi have assisted the government in burying their heads in construction and ignoring foreign affairs, much like the situation of the Soviet Union's efforts in the Five-Year Plan.

Teacher Appointment Letters for Municipal Schools

Must be Issued by the Municipal Bureau of Education

▲Yesterday's Public Notice Informed All Principals and Teachers

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education issued a public notice yesterday, stating that the rules for the appointment and dismissal of teachers in municipal secondary schools and municipal primary schools were revised and promulgated last year. It was also stipulated that after each school plans to hire teachers, it should submit them to the bureau for approval, and the bureau will issue blank appointment letters, fill them out, send them to the bureau for stamping, and return them for transfer. Recently, it has been reported that some primary school principals have hidden the appointment letters issued by the bureau and refused to transfer them, and instead drafted and issued them themselves, which is a violation of laws and regulations. For this reason, this public notice is issued to all principals and teachers of municipal schools. Teacher appointment letters must be obtained using blank appointment letters, filled out, sent to the bureau for stamping, and returned for transfer, so as to show solemnity. This public notice,

Physical Education

Central National Martial Arts Academy Approves

National Martial Arts Teaching Materials for Senior and Junior High Schools

▲First Compile One Semester Each for Senior and Junior High Schools

▲Temporarily Compile Eight Types, to be Completed by Early March

The first meeting of the Teaching Material Compilation and Review Committee of the Central National Martial Arts Academy was held at 2:00 p.m. on January 3 in the conference hall. Attendees included Jiang Rongqiao, Wu Junshan, Huang Bonian, Ma Yongsheng, Luo Chengli, Guo Xishan, Yang Songshan, Gong Runtian, Ma Qingyun, and Jin Yiming. Jiang Rongqiao chaired the meeting, and Jin Yiming served as the recorder. After the ceremony, the chairman reported that the academy had approved the Ministry of Education's request to compile teaching materials for three levels. After investigating national martial arts that meet modern applications, only boxing, sticks, swords, and other types are available. Taking boxing as an example, the postures are different, and the strengths are also different. It is appropriate to go from simple to complex, and from easy to difficult. What should be done should be decided publicly. (1) It was resolved to first compile one semester each of teaching materials for the "junior high school" and "senior high school" levels. After the first phase of teaching materials is compiled, the second semester will be compiled. (2) It was resolved to first determine the names of the teaching materials to be adopted in the first phase of "junior high school" and "senior high school." The names of the teaching materials to be collected in the second phase will be decided after the first phase of teaching materials is compiled. (3) It was resolved that the first phase of teaching materials for junior high schools would be divided into four types: 1. Five Elements Boxing, 2. Tan Tui, 3. Pi Gua Saber, 4. Three Talents Sword. (4) It was resolved that the first phase of teaching materials for senior high schools would be divided into four types: 1. Baji Boxing, 2. Bagua Palm, 3. Plum Blossom Saber, 4. Kunwu Sword. (5) It was resolved that 1. Five Elements Boxing would be compiled by Jiang Rongqiao and Huang Bonian, 2. Tan Tui would be compiled by Ma Yongsheng, 3. Pi Gua Saber would be compiled by Jiang Rongqiao, 4. Three Talents Sword would be compiled by Jiang Rongqiao and Luo Chengli, 5. Baji Boxing would be compiled by Guo Xisan, 6. Bagua Palm would be compiled by Wu Junshan, 7. Plum Blossom Saber would be compiled by Guo Xisan, 8. Kunwu Sword would be compiled by Gong Runtian. (6) It was resolved that the temporary compilation of eight types would be completed before March 1. (7) It was resolved that new martial arts and Qingping Sword, as well as other boxing, saber, and stick methods, would be reserved for review at the next meeting.

▲Hiring National Martial Arts Standardization Committee Members

(Nanjing, 7th) The Central National Martial Arts Academy has approved the Ministry of Education's request to compile national martial arts teaching materials and hire national martial arts masters, as well as experts in medical anatomy, physiology, hygiene, and physical education, to form a National National Martial Arts Standardization Committee. A meeting was held yesterday and decided that the academy's Teaching Material Compilation Committee would be responsible for compiling the teaching materials, and Cheng Fake, Wu Yunrui, Chu Minyi, Shen Kefei, Du Tingxiu, Zhang Xinfu, Jin Yiming, etc., were hired as National Martial Arts Standardization Committee members to jointly prepare and formulate a compilation plan to standardize national martial arts scientifically.

Billiards Performance, Day Two

Smith Becomes Even More Deified

Sets a New Shanghai Record of 670 Points

Liu Fuying and Kang Bosi to Appear Tonight

The highest record of 621 points for a professional billiards player in Shanghai, created by Faulkner, was broken by William Smith with 670 points last night. Smith, a world-renowned professional billiards player, has made the Shanghai Chinese and Western ladies who love this sport feel extremely gratified with his first four performances last night. In particular, amateur players have gained a lot of tips, and the Shanghai billiards community has benefited greatly from Smith. There are two more performances today, and the opponents are Chinese and Portuguese amateur players Liu Fuzong and Kang Bosi. The location and time remain the same.

Smith (right) and Li Gongying (left) in a group photo (photographed by Xu Tianzhang)

Shanghai Record

Smith's two performances on the second day yesterday were even better than the first day. The first game had a total of ten shots and scored 922 points, averaging 92.2 points per shot, which seemed beyond the expectations of the audience. The second game had a total of five shots and scored 1009 points, averaging more than 201 points per shot, which directly surprised the audience. The production of the new Shanghai professional record was also in this last fourth shot. Of the fifteen shots before and after, only the fifteenth shot was a blank shot, presumably because he didn't want to do too much in the last shot. Yesterday's highest score was 670, followed by 527, 241, 228, 88, and 54.

Gongying is Great

Li Gongying, the king of billiards in our country, can compete with world-famous professional players and still show his skills without any anxiety, which is commendable. He took a total of eleven shots yesterday, although he did not produce a huge score, but he had a total of 228 points, averaging more than 20 points, which is particularly commendable for him.

Shizhang is Lovable

Xu Shizhang is a promising young man in our country who represented China as the fifth general in last year's Sino-British International Billiards Championship. He played a few shots last night and showed a lot of potential. The experts also praised him for turning danger into safety several times. His highest score was 24, and he scored a total of 56 points in six shots.

Fuzong Takes the Stage

Liu Fuzong was selected to take the stage at 6:00 p.m. today to compete. Mr. Liu was also one of the five generals in last year's Sino-British International Competition. At 9:15 p.m., it will be the Portuguese master Kang Bosi. At the same time, Smith's performance is getting better and better, and it seems that a higher record can be expected today, refreshing the Shanghai billiards world.

Jiaoda's Farewell Battle in Tianjin

Lost to the China United Team

- One to Two -

▲Two Offsides Result in Loss of Good Opportunities

(Tianjin 5th Dispatch) The Shanghai Jiaoda Football Team, after drawing with Beining at the beginning of the month, met the China team again at Nankai Ground yesterday afternoon. The weather was cold that day, but there were still over a thousand spectators. The ground after the snow was cleared and cleaned, but due to freezing, cracks appeared everywhere on the surface. Before the match, the two armies formed teams and tried out their feet. Although one or two players from the Jiaoda team were still not playing, their strength had been strengthened compared to the battle with Beining. Due to the temporary absence of captain Sun Sijing from the Chinese team, all the team members looked forward to him eagerly. Fortunately, Vice Captain Zhang Changyu arrived at the venue early, and the morale had not been greatly reduced. Therefore, Zhao Qichun was temporarily appointed as the central defender for this match.

The Tianjin team launched a fierce attack at 3:00 PM, and referee Wang Zihua blew his whistle, and the two armies faced off on foot and began to move. The Jiaoda team's front army had excellent connections, but the Chinese team's defense was solid, and they were repeatedly frustrated. Before long, China launched a large-scale attack, and Sun Fulai's ball was extremely fierce, but the goal was deflected. Sun Yongquan rushed up and kicked hard, and the ball crossed the door.

First to score, Jiaoda goalkeeper Fan Jiaju used the opportunity to pass the ball forward to Li Beiliang, but Xue Wenxiu's shot was in vain again. China gained momentum again in an instant, and Zhang Ziyu dribbled the ball forward, and the Jiaoda territory became the target of everyone's attention. Under the trampling of thousands of troops, Jiang Lu cleverly obtained the ball and kicked it smoothly, and the ball rushed to the corner of the net.

Tied score After China got this ball, its prestige became even stronger, and it repeatedly invaded the enemy camp with short-range passes. The Jiaoda defense army did its duty, and Wang Chenlian repelled the enemy army. During the battle, China mistakenly committed a handball, and Li Beiliang took the kick. When his foot rose, he passed it directly to the border. Zhou Guangzhong seized the opportunity to kick it again, and the ball went smoothly into the net. Chen Erde turned around and tried to save it, but it was too late. After fighting for a long time, the first half ended in a 1-1 draw.

Offside pity In the second half, both sides changed generals to respond to the battle, and the battle line changed. After the kickoff, China lost another opportunity. Zhao Qichun echoed back and forth and made a great contribution. Liang Mingzong monitored Wan Xianghua and did not move an inch, which exhausted the young general. The Jiaoda team ran across the entire field, seizing the opportunity to move. Wen Liandong went straight up and attacked the goal urgently, but Jin Adu fell to the ground and caught the ball, and the door was safe again. In an instant, Wan Xianghua had another excellent opportunity to score a goal, but it was a pity that Gong Wenxiu was too eager to advance and was penalized for being offside.

Jiaoda loses Sun Yongquan, the main kicker of the Chinese team, had an excellent landing point. Jiang Lu rushed up and dribbled in, and was surrounded again. Five minutes later, Jiaoda Gong Yibin intercepted the ball shot by Wang Hongrong and quickly kicked the ball, but it worked again, but unfortunately it failed again due to offside. In the last minute, China advanced in unison. Sun Yongquan received the ball passed by Zhang Changyu and took a shot smoothly. It hit the door frame and fell in front of the door. Jiang Lu rushed up and kicked hard, using an excellent posture to win applause again. The game ended in an instant, and Jiaoda lost 1-2. After the battle, Jiaoda team leader Peng Wenyu told reporters that the entire team had set off to return to Shanghai at 10:00 PM last night. Because the team came north a little late and the school will start classes on the 5th, they had to rush back. As for the invitations from friendly teams in various places, it would be difficult to fulfill them. If there is an opportunity in the future, they will come to learn from them again.

Free Talk

Descendants of Prominent Families

— Huang Jiayi

There are only three types of prominent families: First, fathers and grandfathers who read books and became high officials are called prominent families. Their descendants come out refined and elegant, but of extremely high status. They often use a "twist" or say "no," which sweeps everything away. Second, families with military achievements. Although the ancients "disdained taking positions through military merit" or emphasized that "military appearance should not enter the country," that kind of prestige was extremely great among the people. Their descendants dreamed of leading troops into battle, which was extremely terrifying. They could arrest people to be flogged at any time. Third, families that started from business and were also called prominent families were looked down upon by society, but they considered themselves to be in control of society's lifeline. Their descendants felt that anything could be bought. They only asked about the price and exchanged money for it.

Recently, the trend of flogging has decreased. Wealthy young men mostly wear Western suits, and "ladies" also want to be "modern" and walk out on the streets. This is because China has been in a state of "accumulated destruction and misery" for many years and needs equality and freedom.

Taking a closer look at these prominent families, there are only two things inside: barbarism and slavery. In addition, there are some bluffs and attractive signs.

These two spirits are consistent and mutually supportive. The master is a slave because there is an emperor above him and masters above him. There are even more slaves and "slaves of slaves" below him. The consistent policy is to bow and scrape, flatter and ingratiate, which leads to incurable corruption and unrestrained barbarism.

Such a smoky atmosphere envelops the "prominent families," making them "concentrated to the point of being inseparable." The children inside, even if they were originally clever, mostly become vulgar, idiotic, or profligate due to the surrounding environment. Even if they occasionally achieve learning and understanding of human affairs because of wise parents, they simply add a large framework and gilded signs to the outside, with the sole purpose of turning commoners who are not from prominent families into even more miserable slaves.

The stratification of classes in China is not yet obvious, but imagine a commoner walking into a prince's mansion, just like a young diplomat entering the International League of Nations for the first time. They may feel at a loss. This is a good example of class distinction. There are "imperial families" that are more noble than "prominent families," but sometimes there is also the sigh of "I wish to never be born into an imperial family in any lifetime." When slaves rebel, what was once pleasant will mostly become tragic. Using new strength to resist corruption and using civilization to eliminate barbarism are examples with precedents in Eastern and Western history.

In the future, new bureaucratic, warlord, and wealthy merchant "prominent families" will always rise up. Perhaps the attitudes of those descendants will be somewhat different!

On "Lying"

— Yun Gang

Some time ago, I saw Mr. Yu Dafu mention Wilde's "The Decay of Lying" in "Free Talk." That book attacks realism, cherishes the illusory world of beauty in the past, and also says that Americans will not have literary creations, just because the legend of Washington chopping down the cherry tree is a kind of poison that suffocates the creative instincts of Americans.

Although Wilde is called an aesthetic writer and has this kind of view, I actually think that the highest realm of literature is indeed "lying." The fact that photographic art is not as superb as sketching is a fact that has been unanimously recognized since ancient times. Although God's skills are so wonderful, there are still many dull products, so some people say that the artist's skills and creativity sometimes surpass God's. I don't say that, but I think the artist supplements God's lack of skills in creation. Cao Xueqin wrote "Dream of the Red Chamber" and said it was "a tale of nonsense, full of bitter tears." Cao himself admits to lying, but by lying, he shed his sad accumulation. This is the success of lying from the subjective aspect. And because of this lying, "Dream of the Red Chamber" has gained a vast readership. Needless to say, the greatness of the success of lying from the objective aspect is also unquestionable. Even just its "initial opening of chaos" section of stones and grass is beautiful enough! But no one believes that it is not a lie.

The Book of Genesis in the Western Bible is really absurd, but it has become a very powerful part of literature. People do not believe that God's creation of the world was so casual, but don't Adam and Eve often appear in literary works? China also has equally beautiful legends. Not only could Nuwa refine stones to mend the sky, but she could also knead clay to create humans. Unfortunately, Chinese writers, except for a few such as Qu Yuan who were not very "serious," were not very happy to lie. This is also the reason why the field of Chinese literary history is not very glorious.

However, in folk legends, China still has many beautiful lies, such as the story of the White Snake Lady, the transformation of Liang Shanbo and Zhu Yingtai into birds, and Meng Jiangnu who cried down the Great Wall, which can also greatly fill the narrowness of Chinese literary works. In Beiping—that is, ancient Beijing—there are incense mounds and parrot mounds buried in the wild grass near Taoran Pavilion. There are several legends. People who visit and mourn are always lingering there constantly. The not-very-interesting Taoran Pavilion has such one or two mounds, which have added a lot of interest. Someone has to verify that this incense mound is not the tomb of Concubine Xiang, nor is it the place where Lin Daiyu buried flowers; but what is it? It is really what the gentlemen of the "Analects Society" said: "Sugar cake meets a serious person"—who doesn't know that Lin Daiyu is basically a character in "a tale of nonsense"?

Japanese writer Tokutomi Roka, who is now deceased, wrote an excellent book, "Hototogisu," which vividly describes the life of the prodigal son and the places he has been to. Therefore, well-wishers built a temple next to a large tree on the beach of the Sea of ​​Beans. Many writers and young men and women lingered there, leaving behind poems, and there were also paintings like photos. I also visited it, and it seemed very much like it all happened. In fact, it is Roka's lie, at least, most of it is a lie.

The Return Journey

— Dong Meikan

A clear, bright and round moon hung in the dim mid-sky; it was the fifteenth night of the tenth month of the old calendar. The cold wind, like needles, eroded the skin of the travelers on the road, and the streetlights were so tired they were about to doze off. "Let's board the ship!" Yes, I was about to temporarily bid farewell to Shanghai, where I had lived for so long.

Farewell. Just thinking of it brought a touch of sadness. Moreover, moreover, I personally tasted the feeling of having no choice but to be sad? Even though it was only a temporary and short separation.

Quietly I strode onto the ship that pulled people apart. How unsettling were the sounds of the rattling wheels! How could I bear it? My fragile heart was uneasy, involuntarily becoming uneasy!

In the middle of the night, the round moon climbed to the zenith. Solitary loneliness and the sorrow of parting flooded my heart. I just leaned silently against the ship's railing, staring at the deep black, trembling sea; the moonlight spilling over the sea's surface was so faint that it almost made one feel empty! My heart trembled along with the trembling sea waves.

"I might as well leave Shanghai as soon as possible," I thought. However, the ship still lazily lay beside the floating bridge, even though it was groaning. Finally, I became impatient and inquired with the steward about the departure time. How annoying! It was said that there were still three full hours to wait.

People's mood, the mood of parting, is always so strange, feeling both empty and suffocated! The pace of time seemed especially slow at this moment. It was not yet time for the ship to depart. The few passengers in the same cabin, who seemed familiar but had not yet exchanged a word, were all asleep, and sleeping soundly. Their snores arrogantly ridiculed me, tossing and turning without sleep. I couldn't help but feel a sense of jealousy, jealous that they all enjoyed the comfort of sound sleep!

Naturally, I also wanted to find a way to pass this depressing time, but what could I do? Finally, I had to force myself to pick up Dowden's book on Shakespeare and reread it from the beginning. As I read, perhaps because I had recently developed a special interest in Shakespeare, and because it was the second time I had read this book, I was easily drawn into it.

As I looked through it page by page, admiring Shakespeare's greatness, I temporarily forgot that the night was late, forgot the fatigue caused by lack of sleep, and forgot that the ship had already turned and had been sailing for half an hour.

The moonlight seemed fainter than before; it had already passed the zenith. The rattling of the wheels sounded rhythmic; the sea breeze shook the window lattices, and the thin cotton quilt could not withstand the attack of the cold. Although it could not be said that "the cold quilt was like iron," the warmth could be said to have dissipated completely.

I fantasized about meeting my hometown and family, and missed Shanghai and the people in Shanghai that I had just left! In an instant, Shakespeare's shadow became blurred again, leaving only the sentences of the Bard, unconsciously hummed in my mouth, yearning for the scent and shadow of his lover:

"I do not wonder at the whiteness of the lily;

Unless it mar the rose's red!"

The Lying Husband (Continued)

— Zhou Lengjia

In this way, the young husband spent nearly a month in the library. He calculated that the usual payday was approaching, so he ran to several acquaintances to borrow money with a distressed face. Fortunately, he managed to borrow the money, but he was still uneasy. He solemnly instructed each friend, saying that the loan was a secret, and that he would personally repay them as soon as he had the money. He asked them not to go to his home to demand payment under any circumstances.

Presenting the borrowed money to his beloved wife as salary, letting her manage the living expenses, the young husband felt a bitterness in his heart that was even more bitter than coptis. But in order to make his wife happy, he had to force a happy expression, continuing to play the gramophone and chat and laugh with her, even though he was in pain.

However, the power of money is ultimately greater than anything else. Several friends who had lent him money saw that he never came to repay them. Even though they had received his solemn instructions, they had no choice but to go to his home to demand payment for their own needs.

One day, the young husband had just spent the day in the library and returned home. As he reached his door, he suddenly heard the sound of arguing inside the house. He quickly recognized one of the voices as his wife's, and the other as the friend who had lent him money.

"How could this happen? He gets a salary every month, why would he need to borrow money from you?"

"He clearly borrowed it from me. You can ask him if you don't believe me. You can't try to deny the debt! Hmph!"

The young husband instinctively shrank back, tiptoed away from the door, and wandered aimlessly on the street. He didn't return home until it was dark and the electric lights in the stores were shining, estimating that the friend who had come to demand payment must have left. He dragged his tired body home.

As soon as he entered the door, he saw his wife's angry red face, as he had expected. She angrily asked him:

"Did you borrow money from someone?"

The question was like a needle, piercing the young husband's heart, causing him intense pain. He almost couldn't help but cry, but he said with a smile:

"Darling, yes, I did. But these are just small loans, and I can repay him immediately." (The End)

I Curse That Smile of Yours

— Wu Yan

Even now, when I think of that smile, I still want to say fiercely, I curse you!

The incident happened several years ago, but the impression is too deep, always making it difficult to forget, even though I am extremely willing to bury such an unpleasant thing in my heart.

At that time, I was working as a mediocre clerk in an inn in the Savage Mountain, living a life of half-day of hard labor and half-day of teaching.

Every day, when the sun went down, many mule teams carrying goods would come down from the mountain peaks, laden with yellow dust, and spend the night at the shops in the valley. In addition, every few days, there were also Baiyi women from Qianya Dam (called "Yifang Dam" by the Yunnanese), especially many farming girls, carrying local products such as chickens, ducks, geese, eggs, fruits, and some unknown things produced only in the Yi area, passing through here and coming to the mountain shops to rest for a night before going to Bhamo, a large commercial port in northern Myanmar, to exchange them for things like foreign thread, foreign cloth, foreign needles, foreign oil, and foreign matches. They would then pass through here again, stay over, and wait for the morning light of the next day before leaving again with the morning glow.

They walked in groups of twenty or thirty through the Savage Mountain, which had few inhabitants for three or four days, all of it primeval forest. Of course, there were some men mixed in, but the number of men was always small compared to the women. Each person carried two bamboo baskets full of various goods on their shoulders. The way they carried things looked completely different from how the Han Chinese carried things: the bamboo baskets were tied with four ropes, and the ropes were tied to both ends of a carrying pole. They, however, did not need any ropes. They just inserted both ends of the carrying pole into the bamboo baskets and carried them away. In this way, the teams carrying burdens walked slowly in the mountains during the day, talking and laughing, singing songs all the way, with their youthfulness conquering fatigue and hardship.

At noon, they would place their heavy burdens under the trees on the hillside, take out the tin pots from the bamboo baskets, fill them with vegetables and rice, and go to the nearby stream to wash them clean before returning to place them on a stove supported by three stones. At the same time, another female companion would have already gathered an armful of dry branches and fallen leaves from the forest beside the road and come smiling to light the fire.

After the meal, they would re-embark on the familiar journey. Together with the vast twilight, they would enter the thatched shops in the mountain village, and the day's toil would be shed along with the burdens on their shoulders. When they entered the shop, they were as if returning to their own home, without informing the owner or making any polite greetings. Only laughter and voices, along with shadows, would flood in together, rushing to occupy the best rooms and the best sleeping places. Then, they would rush to the kitchen, grabbing the water ladles and competing for the cool water, each tilting back their necks and drinking, laughing.

Our valley was quiet and extremely cold all day long. Especially after noon, everyone would lie down to rest for a while, and there were few people walking outside the shop, making it even more lonely, as if even the surrounding mountains had sunk into the dreams of ancient times. But when they came down from the mountains, the thatched shops in the valley were replaced inside and out by a kind of lively and joyous atmosphere.

After drinking water and resting, these wandering Yi women would each take a clean white towel and go to the stream to bathe. Not until the night had buried the entire valley, with every thatched hut emitting flickering lights, would they return with the cool night air, singing softly and twisting their wet hair. Instantly, the courtyard of the shop was dotted with piles of cooking fires, while melancholy and joyful songs filled the air. The firelight flashed on their slightly red, glowing faces, and the evening breeze blew through their long hair dripping with water droplets. They really seemed like a group of witches suddenly appearing at night, or perhaps water spirits from the river, or forest goblins, come to visit.

There seems to be no need to exaggerate the appearance of these Yi girls, but I want to say a little: having traveled to many places and seen many ethnic groups, it is rare to find anyone as beautiful as the Baiyi women. What surprised me most was that their homes were in the Nujiang River basin and the Binglang River basin (also known as the Olive River and the Taiping River), all places with poisonous miasma where Han people dared not live for long. How could such beautiful flowers grow there? I heard similar remarks in Kunming, and also on the journey to Guangxi:

Gold Market in a Common State

Guangbang's Sales of Bars Decline by $3.80

The gold market trended downward yesterday, with the price outside the market briefly breaking the $700 mark. However, due to the rise in exchange rates, the Hong Kong and Shanghai Bank's listing of sterling was bound to be squeezed. Large investors still had an appetite for buying, so the market situation was relatively stable. The price briefly rebounded midway, but ultimately proved unsustainable due to Guangbang's vigorous selling. The market opened in the morning with news from overseas that the Bank of England had slightly contracted, but the market was bullish on the prospect of a rise, with U.S. banks, forward silver prices, and exchange rates all rising in unison. London spot gold contracted by 9 pence, U.S. cotton rose by 19 points, U.S. wheat rose by 1.25, and stocks fell by half a dollar. The wool market opened at $98.90, then rebounded to $102.30 due to some buyers taking advantage of the low price. After opening, it rose due to the anticipation that the sterling listing would contract by 1.25, but it still declined due to frequent bank sales and Guangbang's forceful selling. The market appeared dull midway. As the domestic market remained loose, Guangbang continued to sell aggressively, and the market closed weaker in the afternoon. There were no special telegrams from Reuters during the morning. People's sentiment was calm. The half-day fluctuation was $4.60, resulting in a decline of $3.80. The price of chih-chih gold was $1,140. The half-day market situation is recorded below:

Securities

Great Efforts by Bulls and Bears

Extremely Few New Trades in Public Bonds

-Market prices rise and fall unevenly-

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange market still trended into chaos. Apart from the exchange period that had some entry and exit, the rest of the new trade was extremely sparse. Both the bullish and bearish sides were tenaciously clinging on, and the majority were prepared to remain waiting for the red plate of the Chinese New Year in order to observe the outcome. In the market, there was exchange, but those were mostly scattered small accounts. To comment on the trend, it is feared that during the Chinese New Year there won't be much fluctuation. There are only two days left for trade. The people in the market mostly expect a good outlook on the red plate. There is also an expectation that the salt tax might discover a new high price above $53. Although this is nonsense and a delusion, if the situation is stable, perhaps there is hope, and not a complete delirium. This prediction is based on the stability of the environment, as well as the continued sale by the bearish side, so it is not without reason. Yesterday passed exceptionally steadily. The trend harmonized on a loop due to chaos. The two morning plates rose before falling, with the number only being one or two points. After the afternoon opening, the rise was insignificantly one point to three points, and because the salt tax rose, it turned into an insignificant rise again. The closing shape was mostly ordinary in the near term and slightly firmer in the distant term. After the salt tax, it seemed slightly tired. The result of market prices was that gains and losses were seen, with the majority being one or two points. The largest fall was in long gold, falling by four points. Cotton Yarn

Major Factories Aggressively Entering the Market

Cotton Yarn Rises by Four Dollars and Seven Cents

The cotton yarn market, which had been sluggish for a long time, suddenly surged by four dollars today. This kind of price increase has not been seen for a long time. Although there was a control association to maintain it last year, the result was not stable. According to rumors in the market, Shenxin Factory, in view of the daily increase in cotton prices and the lack of increase in yarn prices, is facing difficulties. It is said that the factory has purchased several thousand bales in the standard market. At the same time, there are also rumors of offering to buy back "Picking Flower" and "Dragon Boat" yarns from warehouses. This has stirred up people's hearts, and general speculators have followed suit, resulting in a sharp rise in prices.

(Renbiao Steadily Rises) At the opening of the Renbiao market, due to the rise in American cotton, the market was strong, and short sellers covered their positions. Prices for each month rose by one yuan to one yuan and five cents. In the afternoon, it was heard that a certain factory in the front market was buying, with rumors of support. At the same time, buying interest was strong, and prices for each month soared by two yuan and eight cents to three yuan and six cents. The total transaction volume for the day was 39,000 bales. The sales were: Jifeng 1,850 bales, Tongfu 2,250 bales, Yuanda 1,900 bales, Zhenda 1,500 bales, Shenji 1,250 bales, Yichang 2,150 bales, Yongchang 1,850 bales. The purchases were: Suilong 5,500 bales, Hengyi 1,200 bales, Changfeng 2,250 bales, Tonghe 1,000 bales, Xincheng 4,900 bales, Fuda 900 bales, Yuande 750 bales. The closing prices are as follows:

A Large Batch of Indian Cotton Imported

Totaling 7,500 Bales

In recent years, the sales of Indian cotton in China have declined, and imports have gradually decreased. British ships coming to Shanghai from Bombay used to carry cotton as their main cargo, with each shipment being at least 500 to 600 tons, and sometimes as much as 1,000 to 2,000 tons. Now, this has plummeted, reducing the volume to 100 to 200 tons. Due to the poor economic situation in China, according to the local British company yesterday, the company's "Meijie Puer" arrived in port at 3 PM, carrying 7,500 bales of Indian cotton, weighing more than 1,500 tons. This is said to be the largest import of Indian cotton in recent months.

- Rises by About 20 Points in National Currency -

Egyptian cotton spot prices fell by 3 points. The Bombay cotton market fell due to profit-taking by bulls, and the market closed quietly. Grains

The Flour Market Has Equally Strong Bullish and Bearish Forces

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market, the market atmosphere for each month presented an initial appearance of calmness and stability. Although the quotation for foreign wheat fluctuated little, Chicago was better by 48 points, and Canadian wheat was better by about 4 points. However, after the opening, because there was not much activity from factories, outside interests slightly increased their purchases, and people's hearts became firmer. When the market opened in the afternoon, each month was generally hovering. Factories slightly opened up in the current month, while forward months were slightly pulled up. However, since the settlement was approaching, both inside and outside the industry were engaged in closing positions. Although it was heard that the government would import wheat again, about 3,000 to 4,000 tons, and was negotiating with manufacturers, the market's sentiment ultimately saw the bullish and bearish forces as equally matched, and did not see a fall. As a result, the current month was unchanged, March was better by 5%, April was better by 7.5%, May was better by 1%, and June was better by 1.5%, and July was better by 1.75%.

Yin Bian Yuan Alone Falls Slightly

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the sources of supply from various groups were still scarce, totaling nearly 20 dealers, (over 3,000 bags, of which late rice accounted for the majority). The contract sales of out-of-town dealers were also smooth, at over 2,000 bags. As the end of the year is approaching, the market situation is generally flat, and there is already a closing sentiment. Therefore, the prices of Qingjiao, Songsih, and Late Rice remained unchanged. The situation in the local shops was also similar. As a result, Changbang, Su Tong, Nangang, and other Japonica rice, as well as Du - Yangjian, were all fixed. Only Yin Bian Yuan, although it is an important seasonal commodity, ultimately suffered a decline of about a chi due to excessive arrivals and an imbalance between supply and demand, resulting in a dim market color.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, there were 13-14 arriving boats from various groups. The market for each commodity became sluggish, and contract sales were unchanged due to the closing of positions. High-quality Japonica rice was stable, while medium and low grades increased slightly. Bai Yuan, Yang Du, and Bu Jian's prices were firm by several cents. Yin Yuan, Early Bo Rice, and Ke Jian were set.

Soybean Factories Suddenly Intensify Purchases

The Miscellaneous Grains Market has completely closed, but soybeans are still being traded. Yesterday, factories exclusively purchased 12 truckloads of Yingzhou soybeans, with prices opening at 3.45 yuan. There were also export dealers buying 500 bags of Guide soybeans, with prices ranging from 3.55 to 3.53 yuan. The market price was about 2-3% higher than the formal market. The inventory of miscellaneous grains reported yesterday still had omissions, which are recorded below: Tianjin Yellow Soybeans 4,000 bags, Tianjin Green Soybeans 1,500 bags, Chongming Sand Yellow 2,000 bags, Hankou Green Soybeans 2,000 bags, Hankou Sesame 500 bags, and various types of wheat 10,000 bags.

Silk and Tea Huangbai Factory Jing Silk Sales Turn Smooth

▲Japanese Silk Exports Decrease by 30% Last winter, silk industry representatives from various countries held an international silk industry conference in Paris, resolving to restrict the dumping of Japanese silk. It is now learned that the silk weaving industries in countries such as Britain, France, the United States, and India have successively implemented the resolution. Therefore, Japanese silk exports have decreased by 30%. Last month (i.e., January), the total exports of Japanese silk from Yokohama, Kobe, and other export ports were only 80,548 bales.

▲Wuxi Silk Waste Continuously Shipped to Shanghai Recently, silk manufacturers in Wuxi, in view of the launch of overseas silk sales, have been shipping their inventories to Shanghai in batches. In the past few days, silk factories such as Changtu and Tangjian have loaded 340 dan, awaiting sale in warehouses.

▲Factory Jing Silk Sales Turn Smooth Inland silk factories have begun to resume work due to the launch of spring silk sales, and the demand for raw silk has surged. In view of the fact that the prices of Huangbai Factory Jing silk in Shanghai have fallen to the lowest level, they have successively started purchasing, and the transaction volume is not weak. It is estimated that silk merchants in Hangzhou and Shanghai have purchased 80 bales of Huangbai Factory Jing silk, and the price has risen by 30-40 yuan. However, European and American firms are still in the process of negotiating prices, and transactions are pending.

English Keemun Black Tea Sells Well

According to information received by British merchant firms in Shanghai, the London tea market has made significant progress recently. High-grade Keemun black tea from our country, with excellent tea leaves and fragrant aroma, saw exceptionally rapid sales and gradually increasing prices during the turn of December and January. Merchants have made considerable profits. At present, the high-grade inventory has almost been completely sold out. However, low-grade inferior goods, especially low-grade black tea from Hubei and Hunan, have been severely squeezed due to the strong production of Ceylon and Indian tea last year. This kind of market situation of raising the high and suppressing the low is the opposite of what happened at the same time last year.

Metal Company Iron Price Increase Resumes

The metal market has already shown signs of closing, and customers are also busy closing their accounts. The market situation feels quite deserted, so it is very difficult to develop each commodity. However, the Company Iron market, which had been sluggish in the past two weeks, suddenly changed its old appearance in the past two days. Not only was the sales smooth, but the selling price has also soared. It is found that the spot goods are already limited, and the source of supply is also insufficient. People's hearts are extremely firm. Manufacturers such as Huacheng, China, and Tianan have all made purchases, and out-of-town dealers such as Daxincheng are also working hard to collect goods. Therefore, more than 1,400 boxes have been ordered in two days. The price was initially 26.5 yuan, and gradually increased to 28 yuan. The Zhenzhen Laogang factory's goods have even risen to 30 yuan. It is heard that the overseas price is 7.5-7.6 US dollars per box, which is also 2-3% better than before. Therefore, the local standard is expected to rise without falling.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Random Remarks

On the Lunar New Year and the Lunar Calendar

— Wenli

Since the government authorities issued an order to absolutely abolish the lunar calendar and use the solar calendar, people still enthusiastically celebrate the lunar New Year every year. What is the reason for this? The government authorities have gone into considerable detail in implementing the abolition of the lunar calendar and the use of the solar calendar, such as prohibiting government agencies from taking holidays, prohibiting the sale of lunar calendars, and prohibiting the combined use of the old and new calendars on calendars and newspapers. The merchants' seasonal accounts have been changed to four seasons a year, and other methods have been implemented. However, people still follow the old customs and etiquette on festivals and New Years, and regard official orders as mere formalities. Now, let's first discuss what is worth cherishing about the lunar calendar for the people. The twelve months of the lunar year predict the four seasons of climate, spring, summer, autumn, and winter, very accurately. January, February, and March are spring, April, May, and June are summer, July, August, and September are autumn, and October, November, and December are winter. Generally, the climate is more or less mild, hot, cool, and cold, without much deviation. This is the first point. The lunar calendar is very accurate for the phases of the moon, especially the full moon on the fifteenth, and the tides are also very accurate. This is very convenient for people who forget what day it is today. They can immediately know the phase of the moon, whether it is waxing or waning. This is the second point. These two major characteristics of the lunar calendar make it much more convenient for farmers and fishermen to cultivate and go to sea. In addition, the lunar calendar has no advantages in society. Because the solar calendar has become the world's common calendar, now that the sea ban has been lifted and there is frequent communication between China and foreign countries, the solar calendar is more convenient and suitable than the lunar calendar. However, whether it is farmers and fishermen in the countryside or small citizens in the city, they are all "disobeying orders" and using the lunar calendar. In addition to the actual use of the lunar calendar for farmers and fishermen in farming and fishing, small citizens in the city benefit economically from the lunar calendar. The lunar calendar has a leap month every three years, or two leap months every five years. A short month has twenty-nine days, and a long month has only thirty days (solar calendar months have thirty days, and long months have thirty-one days, and only February has twenty-eight days, but this does not happen often, but this year it is twenty-eight days). Merchants settle accounts monthly. In three years, they will have one more month of income. Moreover, the days are shorter, and it is easier to reach the end of the month. Especially for the wage income of shop assistants, how great is the benefit? This is the biggest reason why small citizens in the city insist on preserving and practicing the lunar calendar.

However, many second landlords in Shanghai are also forcing tenants to calculate rent based on the lunar calendar, which is an extra levy by the second landlord on the third tenant. Most third tenants are hardworking families whose lives are not well-off. This extra levy by the second landlord is a considerable loss. For example, a person whose monthly salary is calculated according to the solar calendar pays rent calculated according to the lunar calendar, so he pays one more month's rent every three years. Now that the second landlord is carrying out a rent reduction campaign, the third tenant should also object to this extra levy. The most unreasonable thing is that the apartments in the French Concession are also calculating rent based on the lunar calendar. The author has been subjected to this kind of near-extortion exploitation by second landlords and apartment owners. Now, I am willing to protest to them here on behalf of the exploited. I hope that the second landlords (apartment owners are also a kind of second landlord) will consider that the rent money of poor families also comes from blood and sweat (the money of us writers who sell articles for a living comes from racking our brains). You are carrying out a rent reduction campaign to reduce the burden of life, and the burden of life of the third tenant should also be reduced.

Getting back to the main point, since the lunar calendar is beneficial to the lives of farmers and small citizens, even though the lunar calendar has been abolished, the common people still clearly recognize the scene of "getting rid of the old with the sound of firecrackers" and are unwilling to make mistakes. Political facilities were originally based on the lives of the people. Since the lives of the people require the lunar calendar, even if you issue "repeated orders and injunctions," the habit of "obeying in appearance but disobeying in reality" will not change. If this is a special defect of the people's superstition in practicing the lunar calendar, then there is an error in not understanding social phenomena.

The Anti-Ideal Woman

— Naishuo

Some time ago, I wrote an article on the ideal woman in this publication. Peng read it and criticized me: "You really know so many tricks! But you haven't said enough!" Once, he said: "You've been talking about women for so long, and you still say you're an amateur. I'm going to give you a hard time!" Yesterday, I ran into Miss Yi (who is a disciple of Mr. Liu Bannong, and this is the first time I've called a lady "Miss"). With her gentle demeanor, she launched a campaign to question my nonsense article, saying that it was not only theoretically wrong, but also too insulting to them. Originally, to be honest, that article was indeed nonsense. I couldn't sleep in the middle of the night, or I needed to prepare for the next few days' expenses, so my fingers were a little itchy, and I just made up a bunch of nonsense. It's quite difficult to truly express any great principles in this world. Let's just make up some nonsense. This will only earn me a "degenerate brat" from the so-called revolutionaries, which I don't care about at all.

Getting back to the topic

Miss Yi's first criticism of my mistake was that I paid too much attention to the beauty of women. She said that she was not against beautiful women, but that she could not put the focus on beauty. If you idealize in this wrong way, you will easily get the sorrow of being unable to achieve your goals because reality does not allow it. Because beauty has a standard, you say she is beautiful, but there will be someone more beautiful; and there will be someone even more beautiful above that. And usually beautiful women cannot be completely beautiful. If you want to pursue a completely beautiful woman, then you have to look for her in the realm of fantasy. Only paying attention to the requirements of beauty is a fundamental mistake in the ideal woman. Realistically speaking, beautiful women are very difficult to find. Moreover, a beautiful woman is very difficult to share hardships with. She will often demand a high level of material enjoyment because of her innate beauty. It is always difficult for a modern young man to satisfy her in this regard. Even if he struggles to satisfy her, it is not worth it. Because a woman without sacrifice is a woman without love. And it is extremely unwise to dedicate one's life to a woman without love. Even if a beautiful woman has a good nature, she may not be able to endure hardship together, let alone love you sincerely. Moreover, women with good natures are very few and far between.

The second point is that she also opposed my requirement for gentleness of character, saying that it was tantamount to treating women as attachments, which was a big mistake. Now we must recognize that men simply have no right to make women become parasites or attachments to men. In history and in advanced modern countries, women have shown that they have the same powers and abilities as men. They can control production matters and can undertake other important political and cultural work. Although women in our country are relatively backward, men of the current generation can only help them to gradually share the various affairs of this human society and quickly move towards an equal position in the economy and society. We must never again foster their dependence and turn them into appendages of the family, into canaries that only sing songs.

The third point is that she said that my ideological requirements for women are also fundamentally wrong. She said that I completely wanted to deny the individual existence of women, and only wanted to turn them into a personal plaything. How ashamed should a modern young man be to have this kind of thinking? What right do I have to rely on to treat women like that?

She said that we must never have the mentality of making women appendages or playthings. And we cannot build the ideal woman solely on the point of beauty. In any case, this is a huge mistake. A person's requirements for a woman should focus less on her beautiful appearance, and should pay more attention to her thoughts and character. Regarding the aspect of beauty, we should only require her to have a well-developed, well-proportioned, and healthy female body, and should not require her to have a flower-like appearance. Regarding the aspect of thought and character, we must require her to: first, she should have a firm understanding of society and her personal life; second, she must at least be able to have the skills to live; third, she must have the determination to share a difficult life with you; fourth, she must have her own personality. Not paying attention to her understanding is equivalent to not paying attention to the goal of men and women living together; not paying attention to her living skills is equivalent to not paying attention to the consolidation of the foundation of men and women's lives; not paying attention to her determination to struggle for life is equivalent to not paying attention to the persistence of her love for you; not paying attention to her personality is equivalent to not

Page 20

paying attention to her spiritual help to you. If a person does not pay attention to his ideal woman in this way, it is conceivable that he is ambiguous about other things. Because a contemporary young man, at least, cannot have any comforting hope for life. At least, his life is full of difficulties and struggles.

Finally, she said, "That's why after reading your article, I felt obligated to tell you this. Your desires are completely improper, and are simply like competing with a shadow."

Miss Yi said so much. Although the reasoning is correct, it is actually nonsense like mine. This is truly an "ideal", a "genuine ideal". I really dare not accept it. So, after my face turned slightly red, I only replied with this sentence:

"Miss! Your own ideal is indeed higher than mine!"

In my heart, I was smiling: It turns out that the face and other things of the girl are hundreds of thousands of miles away from my "ideal". Where do I hope for it, to be honest! (End)

On Drinking Alcohol

— A-Dun

Yesterday I discussed alcohol once, and today I want to talk about drinking alcohol again. According to Mr. Zhou Zuoren, although foreigners do not understand the way of drinking tea, they know quite a bit about drinking alcohol. In reality, foreigners' drinking only knows one aspect but not the other.

In essence, there are two ways to drink alcohol, one refined and one crude, one southern and one northern. "The spirit is like a whale sucking up hundreds of rivers," "The throat is like a scorching cauldron, and the breath is like thunder" is crude drinking, which is the northern style. "Sipping gently and drinking slowly" is refined drinking, which is the southern style.

Crude drinking, within the northern style, also has two types. One type is ordinary, with the aim of drinking alcohol, and the other is extraordinary, with the aim of swallowing the "momentum" of the alcohol. The ordinary type is practiced by laborers. After twelve hours of hard work, they buy a packet of peanuts, get four ounces of strong liquor, drink casually, and then leave. The extraordinary type must be heroic men from Yan and Zhao, on the outskirts of the Great Wall with white grass and yellow sand, horses neighing sadly, majestic passes standing tall, holding great power in their hands, swallowing alcohol like whales under the moonlight, burning wild grass and roasting newly caught birds, drinking and singing, in a carefree and generous manner.

Refined drinking, within the southern style, also has two types. However, both are ordinary, and the difference lies in whether the purpose is drinking alcohol. In an empty room with no one, only the sound of falling leaves can be heard. One takes a small cup, slowly pours, and carefully drinks. This is to discern the "taste" of the alcohol. Although one may not necessarily drink a lot, the purpose is in the drinking itself. There is also another type where two or three idlers sit in a hotel, with bare arms and legs crossed. The wine cup barely touches their lips before they put it down again. The purpose of this type is not drinking alcohol but killing time. Even if they raise their cups from time to time, they are merely putting on a show.

For the crude northern style, it is appropriate to use beer or Fenjiu, drinking quickly to get drunk quickly. For the refined southern style, it is appropriate to use rice wine or Shaoxing wine, not necessarily to get drunk, or even not to get drunk at all. Foreigners only know how to swallow wildly, which is clearly crude drinking and not refined drinking, clearly the northern style and not the southern style. Therefore, it is said that "they only know one aspect but not the other."

When drinking alcohol, one should have alcohol in one's eyes, alcohol in one's mouth, and alcohol in one's heart. If not, then one is diminishing the seriousness of alcohol, distorting the meaning of alcohol. Chun Yukun could get drunk with one dou or one shi. When he was drinking alcohol, he was looking at beautiful women, with no alcohol in his eyes and only thoughts of beauties in his heart. Therefore, even if there was alcohol in his mouth, it was not considered alcohol to him. Thus, the capacity of one dou could be used to drink one shi. Naturally, drinking alcohol is materialistic. If there is clearly alcohol being drunk, then whether one gets drunk or not is determined. However, for some people, whether they get drunk or not is determined by their perception. In our hometown, there are people who get drunk just by seeing a wine flag. They come out of their house without drinking alcohol, completely sober. When they see a wine flag, they immediately become slurred and staggeringly drunk. They remain completely drunk all the way until they go back home after drinking their fill. However, as soon as they see their house, they become sober again. This is naturally because they think of the taste of alcohol when they see the wine flag, and they cannot help but feel intoxicated. They think of their wife's face when they see the house, and they cannot help but feel sober. However, this is enough to prove that whether some people get drunk or not is determined by their perception.

Of course, in the above-mentioned ways of drinking alcohol, regardless of which style or type, there is one thing in common, which is that drinking alcohol is voluntary, entirely dependent on one's own pleasure, with no unavoidable reasons. However, in this world, there are actually situations where one must drink. When offered by elders, or when one loses in a drinking game and is penalized with alcohol, that is understandable. During the Wei and Jin dynasties, people took "Wang Shi San" (a type of drug) and could not dispel its effects without drinking alcohol. Therefore, they drank alcohol desperately. At that time, drinking alcohol became a trend. One could not become a famous scholar without drinking alcohol. Even now, there are still literati (regardless of the Shanghai or Beijing style) who use drinking alcohol to show their elegance.

Drinking alcohol can make people forget reality. Therefore, prisoners about to be executed were always given some alcohol to drink. However, among the prisoners, there were those who refused to drink alcohol and wanted to watch the executioner's blade come down clearly. This kind of action really makes the weak feel ashamed. Executioners always drink some alcohol to embolden themselves before execution. So, if they encounter such a prisoner, I really don't know what face they would have to take action.

"Using human heads as wine cups," and they are drinking heartily.

Amateur Mailbox

Look! People with Specialized Skills

Editor:

Every time I read the Amateur Mailbox section in the newspaper, I feel that you are good at answering questions about individual situations and social trends, explaining them clearly and thoroughly, which is truly a pleasure to read! Now I have a significant problem that has been revolving in my mind day and night, and I really can't answer it myself. So, today, I specifically come to ask for your guidance, and I hope you will not hesitate to enlighten me.

I grew up in a place that adheres to the most ancient customs. I studied in private schools from a young age, and after five years of this, I felt that in this era, one must attend school to make progress. So, I entered a higher elementary school. After graduating, I originally intended to continue my studies, but because I wanted to learn some specialized skills and did not want to enter a regular middle school, I continued to study classical texts. After another two or three years of this, I had read all of the Four Books and Five Classics. At that time, some people suggested that I become a teacher, and others suggested that I manage household affairs at home. Because I wanted to learn specialized skills, I did not accept any of these suggestions. Finally, I entered the Provincial Vocational School's dyeing and weaving department, which was very prestigious at the time. After graduating, because the school's machinery was too simple, the school sent me to the provincial First Textile Factory for a six-month internship. Upon completion, because there was no work, the Department of Education introduced me to a famous textile factory in Shanghai. After inspection, I brought my own meals and accommodation and entered the factory for an internship. After about four months, I happened to see that a certain textile factory was recruiting industrial patrol officers, so I took the exam and was fortunately accepted. Thus, I entered the factory for another internship. In this way, I received some allowances each month and interned for another half a year. By the latter half of last year, I no longer had to worry about food and clothing. I thought that my career was settled, and that I only needed to move forward and there would be a way. Who knew that in the 23rd year, my career disappeared, and I became "unemployed." Alas! For the sake of the word "career," I spent five whole years of my precious time and a lot of my family's hard-earned money. Who knew that today, I can't even find a place to go for an internship, and I am drifting in the severe cold and storms thousands of miles away, hungry. Alas! Career, you really harm people!

Editor, in my current situation, how do you suggest I struggle?

Isn't the Ministry of Education now advocating the promotion of vocational schools? Aren't the private middle schools in various provinces going to be converted into vocational schools? May I ask, Editor, where will these batches of vocational students running out of vocational schools go? Wishing you good health! Sincerely, Zhang Shanzhang

Editor's Note: "Career" does not harm people, and "specialized skills" even less so. These not only do not harm people, but they are also things that everyone in society should have. But, Mr. Zhang, what has harmed you? It is this unreasonable society that has harmed you.

This society has reached its end, so "unemployment" is not a strange phenomenon, but rather something that is bound to happen. And for an individual in this society to find a way out for himself, no matter what method he tries to use, the result will probably be useless, except for a few people who have special opportunities. Because the "unemployment" suffering that each individual in the current society experiences is mostly not due to his own shortcomings, but rather driven by the flaws in the social system. Therefore, it is beneficial to both the individual and society for an individual to serve society and survive in society with specialized skills. However, before the root cause of the "society's" illness is removed, specialized talents cannot avoid the danger of decline. Unemployment is not an individual's problem, nor can it be avoided by individual efforts, but rather a problem of the entire society, which needs to be solved by the transformation of the entire society. Therefore, if the entire society has a way out, then individuals will also have a way out. Otherwise, relying solely on individual efforts is like buying lottery tickets, and while there are people who win prizes, they are very few.

For Mr. Zhang's current livelihood, the only way is to seek employment as much as possible. If there is no one to introduce him, then he can register with the China Vocational Education Society and submit a letter to the Self-Employment Introduction column in this newspaper's supplement to seek employment. This is a way of "doing one's best," but I dare not say whether it will be effective.

Brother Mao and Sister Bao Travel the World

Novel

The Lonely Man (9)

— Dai Ni

(5) Night Talk

A few days after Kejia and Jingyi got married. The days of spring fly by so quickly, please forgive me for not remembering exactly how many days it was, but in fact, it wouldn't matter much even if I remembered clearly.

Jingwen's mother had already moved into the new house, fulfilling the jest of "Mom and younger sister getting married together." She herself was busy every day, saying that she definitely wouldn't go back to Hangzhou to be an unschooled teacher. Her daily travels were all for the sake of finding someone to continue her position. Xiaoxun was living a contradictory life. He disliked Shanghai, yet he also loved Hangzhou, just like he loved Shanghai. It seemed that when he was happy, it didn't matter where he lived. Kejia wanted him to live in the new house, so he moved in without any objections.

One evening, Jingwen sent her replacement to Hangzhou, and the people here were chatting in the "spring-filled" new room. Kejia and Jingyi were snuggled together, sitting side by side on the sofa. The old lady was leaning against the bed, she was always smiling -- a kind middle-aged woman. Xiaoxun was sitting on the writing desk, one leg supporting the ground, the other leg resting on his knee, swinging it. Everyone was cracking melon seeds, seizing every opportunity to say witty remarks without a purpose.

"Why do most of the melon seed shells that are spat on the ground face upwards?" Xiaoxun asked triumphantly.

Six pairs of eyes simultaneously shot towards the floor.

"It is said to be a sign of courtship, women often hold back in that way, ignoring men."

"Is our little sister like that?" Clearly, this was a good opportunity to say something witty, and Xiaoxun seized it. Jingyi's mouth drooped downwards, and she pushed Kejia with a charming push, as if saying "Look, he's taking advantage of me." However, she refused to admit defeat: "Yes! This can make a man heartbroken."

She bit her lip, her gaze pausing from Kejia's mother's face to Xiaoxun's face, and the three of them laughed at the same time. Xiaoxun also forced a smile, stopped the leg that was swinging on his knee, and stared at the melon seed shells on the ground in a daze. The March spring breeze blew in from the window, stirring his naturally wavy hair.

A clever woman understands everything, a clever man also understands everything; naturally, a clever middle-aged woman understands even more. At this time, the old lady slightly raised her voice and said:

"The two sisters are really the same. Talking without thinking." She turned her head back, "Isn't Mr. Zhu preparing to marry a wife because of Miss Xu?" The old lady deliberately said with a smile, so as not to make her words edged.

"What are you talking about? Auntie." Xiaoxun shook his naturally wavy hair, "No woman wants to marry me!" He also deliberately said with a smile, seemingly wanting to steer the topic away.

"Humph!" Jingyi blurted out, "Waiting for Qin Hu to get divorced?"

It seemed as if no one had expected it, and they stopped talking, stopped cracking melon seeds. Xiaoxun reached behind him and took out a cigarette from the cigarette can on the writing desk, lit it, and the white smoke drifted out of the window with the spring breeze, lightly. The old lady stood up and yawned.

"I wonder when Jingwen will be back, I want to go to sleep." Saying that, she walked out on her own. The clock struck ten.

"Brother," Kejia moved his body forward, looking very serious, "What is Qin Hu's attitude exactly?"

"What attitude?" He exhaled a puff of smoke, and the leg resting on his knee began to swing.

"Seeing her attitude that day... attitude..." He was not familiar with the appropriate wording for that kind of thing, his body falling back onto the sofa, looking at Jingyi, naturally asking for help.

"You talked a lot that day, right?" Calmly, preventing a nervous reaction.

"Yes. We took a lap around Nanjing Road that day, and divorcing the young master is something to be expected. She left me to marry this capitalist's husband, so she wouldn't still be clinging to someone as insignificant as me. But she said that the young master is not a good person, and expressing intimacy with me is to need me to be a puppet once more. Jingyi's words guessed one aspect of her, do you think I'm that kind of person?"

He laughed nervously, the laughter so unpleasant, like an owl in the middle of the night. He flicked the cigarette bud out the window, his body sliding from the writing desk into the writing chair.
