Film Supplement

Dario's Predictions: Hollywood's Trends This Year (Part 2)

— Bing

Garbo will leave the film industry forever

Fairbanks will return to Hollywood

Mary Pickford's fate is also covered in clouds. Especially at the end of the year, she will encounter many thorns. She will engage in writing thereafter; within two years, she will complete a very valuable memoir. This year she will produce a film, but this film may not be outstanding.

Constance Bennett will have high luck this year, and she will have amazing developments. There is no possibility of her getting divorced this year. She needs to pay special attention to her health, especially she should avoid undergoing surgery.

German star Leni Riefenstahl will return to Europe this year. The above is our abridged translation of the fate of the top ten actresses this year. Now let's see how things will change on the male stars' side.

John Barrymore's luck is average. His works continue to be successful. His family life is happy, and he will have a son.

What about Lionel Barrymore? He will encounter great danger this year. Clouds cover his luck.

John Gilbert's luck is not bad. Either this year or next year, he will have twins, and they will be daughters. He has no son in his fate.

Clark Gable's health is still not improving. But he will hold a wedding.

Charles Farrell will once again show his talents on the screen this year. His marriage problems will also be resolved satisfactorily. The dangerous period has passed!

Edmund Lowe and Lilyan Tashman are best off not flying this year. Otherwise, the result will be either injury or crippling of one or both legs.

Gary Cooper will still have to live a single life this year. He will be frightened by flying this year.

He will soon make a fortune -- but it will definitely not come from acting, mostly from oil mines.

Fairbanks will suffer some bad luck and will lose his health. He will return to Hollywood from England.

Douglas Fairbanks Jr. will also return to Hollywood. According to the crystal ball, if he gets married this year, the marriage will still not have good results. He had best find a woman outside the film industry.

Adolphe Menjou will get married again this year. This time his wife will be a woman outside the film industry. This time they can live together until old age.

Charlie Chaplin will produce a valuable film this year. He is about to marry Paulette Goddard. This marriage will definitely remain very happy this year. But if not, there will be many disputes this year.

In addition to the predictions about the lives of movie stars, Daario also gave considerable instructions on the trends of the entire Hollywood film industry. He said that the American film industry has a tendency to recover and prosper this year. Many new companies and many new stars will emerge this year. (The End)

Film Reviews

Review of "The Chief"

— Ling He

The Chief

A character who enjoys great fame on the radio station is actually used by the producer as a drawing point on the screen, which is not excessive in terms of business competition. Just like China's Wang Wu Neng or Jiang Xiaoxiao, going from the stage to the screen, aren't they also receiving great welcome? In addition, "The Mad Musketeer" also featured the great singer Chaliapin, who caused a sensation on the screen for a while. Therefore, Edwin also moved from the radio station to the screen.

In the stories told by Edwin on the radio station, there was this "The Chief", which was quite praised by people. In this story, he humorously satirized the so-called hero.

The so-called Henry is the head of the fire brigade who died in the line of duty. The citizens were grateful for his virtue and added the name of the hero's son to Henry. However, Henry is actually not a hero. On the contrary, he is just a clumsy and honest mediocrity. However, Edwin also made him establish special merit in a chance encounter. These chance encounters are naturally used as material for laughter. He fights with bears, and he makes faces with monkeys. Similarly, there are also many people who use his name as a tool for campaigning, and there are also people who harm his mother because he is their political enemy. As a result, this hero, in order to rescue his mother, calls for votes for the cunning politicians.

In the midst of this, he sharply satirized this hero, and at the same time, he sympathized with the hero's honest heart, and even explained that he would not wear a gentleman's top hat and evening dress. And such a hero is always used by bureaucratic politicians. Isn't that right? You can treat him as any kind of puppet, and he will not feel this ineffable sadness. This so-called hero is both pitiful and laughable. In this way, "The Chief" has its own profound meaning.

But in terms of performance, it is not seen how successful it is. Edwin's performance does not match the brilliance of the story, although his tone of dialogue is very worthy of people's attention.

As for the director's technique, there is nothing special to commend. The most worthy of mention is the transition from a static atmosphere to a climax. When Henry discovered his mother being robbed in the middle of the night, the climax began as he called out "Mom" loudly. Then came Henry's anxious arrival at his company, followed by his mother's peaceful conversion of the bandits, and then Henry's madness, running madly through the streets and shouting. This one climax ends the story. Although this is not popular with Chinese audiences when the program returns to the main topic on the radio station, it is precisely Edwin's purpose.

Even so, this is not an outstanding achievement in American comedy films, but it is still passable.

The Ladies Man

— Li Man

Facing the Music is Showing in Shanghai

"The Ladies Man" is another empty and boring musical comedy.

Therefore, we inevitably have to use the old tricks, affected affectation, senseless chases, and absurd jokes... The story only has three sentences. Young Jacques sees the beautiful young lady Vina in the theater, so he tries every means to pursue her, and finally achieves his ultimate goal.

Here, Stan Laurel has stumbled several times, bumped into twenty or so strangers, broke eight or nine bottles, and hid six or seven times under the sofa in a pile of fur... These, these, are what consumed all the film of "The Ladies Man".

However, the director Harry Hughes's handling is commendable here. He has handled the music, songs, and humorous movements harmoniously. In the final scenes, dancing is on stage, and Stan Laurel and the thieves are chasing each other off stage. He handled it in an orderly manner, first a shot of the dancing on stage, then Stan Laurel and others secretly taking their seats, then a shot of the dancing on stage, then Stan Laurel's escape and the thieves' pursuit, then the dancing on stage again, and so on...

And there are also some places that are handled very concisely, such as the orderly pace of the army on the street, to the pace of the actors indoors, and the singing of the actors on stage, etc. in several scenes.

The following places:

(1) Stan Laurel flips through the phone book, looking for fabricated names.

(2) Vina shows Jacques the book "This is to Love", and Jacques gives Vina the book "Hold my Heart".

Compared to the other scenes, these are more vivid and natural. As for the rest, like "The Great Ziegfeld" and other musical comedies, everything is forced, boring, absurd, and unreasonable, even though "Faust"'s "Jewel Song" is used to attract viewers here.

As for the performance, Stan Laurel's ability to make a commotion is worth mentioning, but at most, like Roscoe Arbuckle, Laurel and Hardy, etc., besides temporarily making the idle open their mouths to laugh, he cannot give us some of the deeper meaning that Charlie Chaplin gives us.

Nancy Burn, who plays Vina, performed very well.

Douglas Fairbanks: One Reason for His Decisive Departure

— Fu

The immensely famous Douglas Fairbanks has left his domain of Hollywood, left his beautiful wife Mary Pickford, and gone to London, England. Some are saying he will not return to Hollywood. Perhaps he will even establish a British film company to compete with American films. Consequently, people generally feel that even if Douglas Fairbanks is not guilty of any treasonous behavior, there must be a rift between him and the American film industry that caused him to be dissatisfied and depart decisively.

But what is the reason for this decisive departure? This is very difficult to know. Even if someone knows, they would never dare to make it public in the newspapers, because America is still hoping for his return. Even if this martial arts star has become a figure of the past in the American film industry, the American film industry would never lightly let him defect to the enemy's side. But why is Fairbanks so resentful towards the American people in general?

It is said that he does not have any deep-seated hatred towards the American film industry. However, he is very resentful of the American social circles for having once slighted him. This may be one reason he is seeking glory abroad. American society (Society) is inherently extremely strict. They are a small circle of the highest class, into which not only people without money or status cannot squeeze, but even the nouveau riche can only sigh in despair. After Douglas Fairbanks became famous in the film industry, he very much wanted to squeeze into the social circles of Santa Barbara, California. However, those social figures were unwilling to open their doors and let Hollywood figures in. Therefore, Fairbanks left in a fit of anger. When he and Mary arrived in London, the British King even granted them an audience.

Whether this is the reason for the rift between Fairbanks and the social circles of his own country is unknown. But the occurrence of this event is indeed real.

Film Novel

Queen Christina (7)

— Hu Chen

The young special envoy, hearing the innkeeper's words, happily said, "It would be wonderful if I could find a place to stay tonight." The innkeeper then said to Christina, "Sir, your room is the best in our inn... I wonder if it would be possible to ask you to share a room with this gentleman for one night..." Christina's breathing became a little short. Her eyebrows rose. The young special envoy saw this and said to her, "Sir, I should not force you, but..." He smiled, and Christina's heart could not help but skip a beat. The young special envoy looked at her very earnestly and said, "I feel there is much more to talk about..." Christina said, "It would be very interesting to talk to you..." Her eyes darted around and she did not continue. The innkeeper felt that she had yielded a little, so he intervened from the side. The young special envoy added, "I can talk to you all night. I can also say nothing at all. Whatever you command... What I ask for is not just a bed—I also want to talk to you about home!"

Christina looked at him, feeling very embarrassed. Finally, she said softly, "I would rather give up the room and warm myself by the fire here." The young man's face showed an expression of shame. "Does my politeness displease you? Do my words tire you? If you find me too boring, please forgive me." As he said this, he stood up, bowed deeply, and said goodnight to Christina; he was about to leave. Christina quickly called him back, and the young man sat down again. He said, "Let's not talk about this matter. It's fine for me to warm myself by the fire here tonight." Christina quickly stopped him; "No, no, I can't let you warm yourself by the fire here alone, I'll share the room with you." The young man, as if afraid that she would change her mind, quickly stood up and thanked her, and put an arm around Christina's petite shoulder, expressing affection, "I will do my best to make you happy."

The innkeeper, looking on, was extremely pleased and immediately led the two of them upstairs to the room, where a very flirtatious maid was kneeling on the floor, taking off their boots for them. After a while, the maid left, leaving the two of them alone in the room. They looked at each other, each feeling a strange and inexplicable emotion surging in their chest. Finally, the young Spaniard spoke, "My name is Don Antonio Yous, Miguel, Trapera du, Duke of Bivondele (full name), special envoy of King Philip of Spain, Aragon, Castile (Spanish territories)." After he finished speaking, he waited quietly for Christina to announce her official title and name. Christina hesitated for a moment, then reluctantly said, "I am the Duke of Du Hao." The young special envoy stood in front of the large mirror and began to take off his clothes, but he suddenly stopped. He said very boredly, "You must come to Spain to travel." Christina replied solemnly, "I would very much like to go." The young special envoy said, "You can stay in my residence, you can..." He suddenly stopped again, feeling that indescribable emotion preventing him again. (To be continued)
